Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony of an Uncircumcised Person: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on testimony of an uncircumcised person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of an uncircumcised person and explain the condition under which it is rejected.

Core Idea
An uncircumcised person's testimony is accepted unless the omission is out of contempt for religion.

In Islamic legal procedure, the integrity ('adalah) of a witness is crucial. This lesson examines a specific case: the testimony of an uncircumcised male. The Hanafi school, considering circumcision a sunnah, generally accepts such testimony, distinguishing between legitimate omission and contemptuous disregard. Understanding this ruling reveals the school's approach to evaluating witness credibility based on religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Read the matn: the testimony of an aqlaf (uncircumcised) is accepted. Note the default hukm: accepted (sahih).
The default is acceptance, not rejection.
2
Locate the exception
The exception is when the person leaves circumcision out of contempt (istikhfaf) for religion. This changes the ruling to rejection.
Contempt indicates weakness in faith, which destroys 'adalah.
3
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The reasoning: circumcision is sunnah in the Hanafi school. Leaving a sunnah does not impair 'adalah unless done with contempt. Contempt makes the person non-'adl, even non-Muslim.
The proof is based on the graded nature of obligations: sunnah vs. wajib.
4
Compare with opposing schools
Identify that Shafi'is and Hanbalis consider circumcision wajib. For them, leaving a wajib may affect 'adalah. Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The disagreement is rooted in the classification of circumcision.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario: a man is uncircumcised due to medical reasons, his testimony is accepted. If he openly mocks circumcision, his testimony is rejected.
The key is the intention behind the omission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتقبل شهادة الاقلف لانه لا يخل بالعدالة الا اذا تركه استخفافا بالدين لانه لم يبق بهذا الصنيع عدلا
ترجمہ اور غیر متون کی شہادت مقبول ہو سکتی ہے کیونکہ یہ اس کی عدالت میں مخل نہیں ہے مگر جب اس نے اس کو دین میں حقیر سمجھ کر چھوڑا ہو کیونکہ وہ اس حرکت سے عادل نہیں رہے گا۔
تشریح اقلف غير مختون ، بے ختنہ، ختنہ ہمارے نزدیک سنت ہے اور اس کے قائل امام مالک ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک واجب ہے۔ ختنہ کے لئے امام ابو حنیفہ نے کوئی وقت مقرر نہیں فرمایا ہے۔ البتہ متاخرین نے سات سال سے دس سال تک کا وقت مقرر کیا ہے۔ اور بعض نے ولادت کے ساتویں دن یا ساتویں دن کے بعد کو متعین کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ حسنین کی ختنہ ولادت سے ساتویں دن ہوئی یا ساتویں دن کے بعد ہوئی اور بعض نے کہا کہ بچہ جب دسویں سال میں ہو تو اس کی ختنہ کی جائے گی۔ بہر حال صاحب قدوری رقم طراز ہیں کہ غیر مختون کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی اس لئے کہ ختنہ ہمارے نزدیک سنت ہے اور ترک سنت عدالت میں مخل نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا ختنہ کا نہ ہونا اس کی عدالت میں مخل نہ ہوگا اور جب غیر مختون ہونا اس کی عدالت میں مخل نہیں ہے تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول ہو گی۔ ہاں اگر سنت سے اعراض کر کے دین کو حقیر سمجھ کر اس نے ختنہ کو ترک کیا ہے تو یقیناً اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کیونکہ وہ اس حرکت سے عادل کیا مسلمان بھی باقی نہ رہا۔ اور جب عادل نہ رہا بلکہ مسلمان ہی نہ رہا تو اس کی گواہی کس طرح قبول ہو سکتی ہے لیکن اگر کسی عذر کی وجہ سے ختنہ کو ترک کیا ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول ہوگی.
He said: The testimony of an uncircumcised person (aqlaf) is accepted because it does not affect 'adalah, except when he leaves it out of contempt for the religion, because he does not remain 'adl by this action. (Translation:) And an uncircumcised person's testimony can be accepted, because it does not affect his 'adalah, except when he left it considering it contemptible in religion, because he will not remain 'adl by this action. (Tashreeh:) Aqlaf means uncircumcised. Circumcision according to us is sunnah; Imam Malik also holds this view. According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, it is wajib. Imam Abu Hanifa did not fix a specific time for circumcision. However, later scholars fixed a time from seven to ten years. Some fixed it on the seventh day after birth or after, because the circumcision of Hasan and Husayn was on the seventh day or after. Some said the child should be circumcised when he reaches ten years. In any case, al-Quduri writes that the testimony of an uncircumcised person is accepted, because circumcision according to us is sunnah, and leaving a sunnah does not affect 'adalah. So not being circumcised does not affect his 'adalah, and when being uncircumcised does not affect his 'adalah, then his testimony is accepted. However, if he left circumcision out of disregard for the sunnah and contempt for the religion, then certainly his testimony will not be accepted because by this action he did not remain 'adl, rather he did not even remain a Muslim. And when he is not 'adl and not even a Muslim, how can his testimony be accepted? But if he left circumcision due to an excuse, his testimony will be accepted.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the testimony of an uncircumcised male (aqlaf). The Arabic matn (from al-Quduri) states that his testimony is accepted because uncircumcision does not affect his legal integrity ('adalah), except if he deliberately avoids circumcision out of contempt for the religion, which would undermine his 'adalah and even his faith. The Urdu commentary expands by noting the status of circumcision (khitan) across the schools: in the Hanafi school it is sunnah (while Shafi'is and Hanbalis consider it wajib). Since leaving a sunnah does not impair 'adalah, the testimony is generally accepted. However, if the omission stems from contempt (istikhfaf), it indicates a lack of religious commitment that discredits the witness. The commentary also mentions the recommended age for circumcision according to later Hanafi scholars, though Imam Abu Hanifa himself did not specify a time.

Key Terms
اقلف (aqlaf): An uncircumcised male.
ختنہ (khitan): Circumcision; the removal of the prepuce.
استخفاف بالدین (istikhfaf bi al-din): Treating religion with contempt; deliberately deeming religious practices insignificant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what circumstance is the testimony of an uncircumcised person rejected in the Hanafi school?
A) Whenever he is uncircumcised.
B) Only if he is uncircumcised due to a medical excuse.
C) Only if he left circumcision out of contempt for the religion.
D) Only if he is above ten years old and uncircumcised.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of an uncircumcised person is accepted in the Hanafi school because circumcision is sunnah, but it is rejected if the omission stems from contempt for religion.

Testimony of a Eunuch: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof from Umar's practice and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a eunuch and cite the primary evidence from the practice of Umar (ra) and the supporting analogy.

Core Idea
A eunuch's testimony is accepted in Hanafi law — physical defect does not impair legal credibility.

The testimony of witnesses is a cornerstone of Islamic judicial procedure. One specific question is whether a physical condition like castration disqualifies a witness. This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar establishes the Hanafi position that a eunuch's testimony is valid, using both a precedent from Umar ibn al-Khattab and a reasoning by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the statement: 'And the eunuch (khasi)... his testimony is accepted.' Determine the hukm level: is it sahih, fasid, or batil? Note that the ruling is about the permissibility of acceptance.
The ruling is that his testimony is accepted (maqbul), meaning it is sahih in terms of admissibility.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites 'Umar accepted the testimony of Alqamah al-Khasi.' This is a qawl sahabi (Companion's practice) used as evidence. Identify the Companions involved and the context (case of Qudamah ibn Maz'un).
Umar's action is a form of Sunnah (fi'li) and is binding in Hanafi usul when not contradicted.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does Umar's acceptance prove the rule? Because he did not question Alqamah's qualification due to his condition; thus castration does not affect 'adalah (integrity).
The straightforward implication is that a eunuch is like any other free male Muslim of integrity.
4
Examine the secondary proof (qiyas)
The matn says: 'And because a limb was cut from him unjustly, so it is as if his hand was cut.' Understand the analogy: just as a person with a severed hand can testify, so can a eunuch. The effective cause (illa) is that neither condition affects one's moral character or ability to observe and report.
This qiyas reinforces the ruling but the primary evidence remains Umar's practice.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
Synthesize: The testimony of a eunuch is accepted in the Hanafi school, as stated in the Zahir al-Riwayah. The ruling is based on clear precedent and sound analogy.
This is the mufta bihi position; there is no known intra-Hanafi dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والخصى فان عمر رضى الله عنه قبل شهادة علقمة الخصى ولانه قطع عضو منه ظلما فصار كما اذا قطعت يده
ترجمہ اور خصی کی گواہی قبول ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت عمر نے علقمہ خصی کی گواہی قبول کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ خصی کا ایک عضو ظلماً کا نا گیا ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ ہاتھ کاٹا گیا ہے۔
تشریح خصی و شخص ہے جس کے خصیتین نکال دیئے گئے ہوں ۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ خصی کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے۔ اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے قدامہ بن مظعون کے خلاف شراب پینے کے سلسلے میں عالقمہ خصی کی گواہی قبول کی ہے۔ قدامہ بن مظعون صحابی ہیں غزوہ بدر اور دیگر تمام غزوات میں شرکت کی ہے۔ عبداللہ بن عمرؓ اور حفصہ بنت عمر کے ماموں ہیں ۔ حضرت عمرف
He said: And the eunuch (khasi), Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) accepted the testimony of Alqamah al-Khasi. And because a limb was cut from him unjustly, so it is as if his hand was cut. (Translation:) And the testimony of a eunuch is accepted. Because Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) accepted the testimony of Alqamah al-Khasi, and because a limb of the eunuch was cut off unjustly, so it is as if his hand was cut. (Tashreeh:) A khasi is a person whose testicles have been removed. Al-Quduri said: The testimony of a eunuch is accepted. And the evidence is that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) accepted the testimony of Alqamah al-Khasi in the case of Qudamah ibn Maz'un regarding drinking wine. Qudamah ibn Maz'un is a Companion who participated in the Battle of Badr and all other battles. He is the maternal uncle of Abdullah ibn Umar and Hafsa bint Umar. Umar (may Allah be pleased with him)...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the testimony of a eunuch (khasi). The Arabic matn (from al-Quduri) says that a eunuch's testimony is accepted, citing two proofs: first, the practice of Umar (ra) who accepted the testimony of Alqamah al-Khasi in the case of Qudamah ibn Maz'un (who was accused of drinking wine); second, by analogy (qiyas): the removal of testicles is like the cutting off of a hand – and a person with a severed hand is not disqualified from giving testimony. The Urdu commentary elaborates on the background: Qudamah ibn Maz'un was a prominent Companion and the maternal uncle of Abdullah ibn Umar and Hafsa. The acceptance of Alqamah's testimony by Umar establishes the permissibility of accepting testimony from a eunuch, as the condition of 'adalah is unaffected by the loss of a limb.

Key Terms
خصی (khasi): A eunuch; a male whose testicles have been removed.
علقمہ خصی (Alqamah al-Khasi): A Companion known by this name; his testimony was accepted by Umar in a case against Qudamah ibn Maz'un.
قدامہ بن مظعون (Qudamah ibn Maz'un): A Companion and maternal uncle of Abdullah ibn Umar and Hafsa; he was accused of drinking wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling that a eunuch's testimony is accepted?
A) A direct Quranic verse.
B) The practice of Umar (ra) accepting the testimony of Alqamah al-Khasi.
C) Consensus of all schools.
D) Analogy with the testimony of a blind person.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a eunuch is accepted in the Hanafi school, established by the precedent of Umar and reinforced by qiyas.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Testimony of a Eunuch (al-Khasi)
Ruling on accepting testimony of a eunuch

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a eunuch and distinguish between unjust and voluntary castration.

Core Idea
A eunuch's testimony is accepted if castrated unjustly; if voluntary, it is rejected.

This lesson examines a specific issue in the law of testimony (shahadat): the acceptance of a eunuch's testimony. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of Caliph Umar and a qiyas analogy, holds that unjust castration does not impair a person's 'adalah. However, if the castration was voluntary, it is a sin that disqualifies the witness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the ruling from al-Quduri: the testimony of a eunuch (khasi) is accepted.
The matn says 'wa al-khasi' and the commentary confirms acceptance.
2
Examine the first proof
Analyze the practice of Caliph Umar: he accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch in the case of Qudamah ibn Maz'un. This is a sunna of the rightly-guided caliph, considered hujja by Hanafis.
The incident is narrated to show that Umar saw no defect in the eunuch's testimony.
3
Examine the second proof
Understand the qiyas: a eunuch's testicles were cut off unjustly, similar to a person whose hand is cut off unjustly. In both cases, the limb removal does not affect 'adalah, so testimony is accepted.
The analogy is based on the common illa: cutting off a limb unjustly.
4
Note the exception
Identify the key condition: if the eunuch voluntarily removed his own testicles, his testimony is rejected because it is a sinful act that impairs 'adalah.
The text says 'if someone willingly and voluntarily removed his own testicles, then his testimony is not accepted.'
5
Understand the principle
General principle: unjust oppression does not negate 'adalah. Therefore, victims of unjust mutilation remain reliable witnesses.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on actual moral integrity rather than physical perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والخصى فان عمر رضى الله عنه قبل شهادة علقمة الخصى ولانه قطع عضو منه ظلما فصار كما اذا قطعت يده ترجمہ اور خصی کی گواہی قبول ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت عمر نے علقمہ خصی کی گواہی قبول کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ خصی کا ایک عضو ظلماً کا نا گیا ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ ہاتھ کاٹا گیا ہے۔ تشریح خصی و شخص ہے جس کے خصیتین نکال دیئے گئے ہوں ۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ خصی کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے۔ اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے قدامہ بن مظعون کے خلاف شراب پینے کے سلسلے میں عالقمہ خصی کی گواہی قبول کی ہے۔ قدامہ بن مظعون صحابی ہیں غزوہ بدر اور دیگر تمام غزوات میں شرکت کی ہے۔ عبداللہ بن عمرؓ اور حفصہ بنت عمر کے ماموں ہیں ۔ حضرت عمر نے ان کو بحرین کا عامل مقررفرمایا تھا مگر پھر معزول فرما دیا تھا۔ مختصر واقعہ یہ ہے کہ عبدالقیس بن البحرین کے سردار جارود نے قدامہ بن مطعون کے خلاف گواہی دی کہ یہ شراب پیتا ہے۔ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا کہ کیا تیرے ساتھ کوئی دوسرا گواہ ہے۔ علاقہ خصی نے کہا کہ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ میں نے اس کو شراب پیتے ہوئے دیکھا ہے۔ اس کے بعد حضرت عمر نے اپنے بہنوئی قدامہ کو کوڑے لگوائے اور ان کو معزول کر دیا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ خصی کا عضو ( خصیتین ) ظلماً کاٹا گیا ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کس کا ہاتھ کا نا گیا ہو۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ اگر کسی کے تمام اعضاء ظلما کاٹ دیئے گئے ہوں تو اس سے اس کی عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوتی اور جب عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوئی تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول کر لی جائے گی ۔ ہاں اگر کسی نے برضاء ورغبت اپنا خصیہ نکال ڈالا ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
He said: And the eunuch—for Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch, and because a limb of his was cut off unjustly, so it becomes as if his hand were cut off. Translation: And the testimony of a eunuch is accepted, because Umar accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch, and because a limb of the eunuch was cut off unjustly, so it is as if his hand were cut off. Commentary: Khasi is a person whose testicles have been removed. The author of al-Quduri said that the testimony of a eunuch is accepted. The proof is that Umar accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch in the matter of Qudamah ibn Maz'un regarding drinking wine. Qudamah ibn Maz'un is a Companion who participated in Badr and all other battles; he is the maternal uncle of Abdullah ibn Umar and Hafsa bint Umar. Umar had appointed him governor of Bahrain but later dismissed him. The brief incident: Jarud, the chief of Abd al-Qays from Bahrain, testified against Qudamah that he drinks wine. Umar asked, 'Do you have another witness?' Alqamah the eunuch said, 'I testify that I saw him drinking wine.' Then Umar had his brother-in-law Qudamah flogged and dismissed him. The second proof is that the eunuch's limb (testicles) was cut off unjustly, so it is as if his hand were cut off. And it is well-established that if one's limbs are cut off unjustly, his reliability is not nullified, and when reliability is not nullified, his testimony is accepted. Yes, if someone willingly and voluntarily removed his own testicles, then his testimony is not accepted.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the testimony of a eunuch (khasi). The matn from al-Quduri rules that his testimony is accepted, citing two proofs: first, the practice of Caliph Umar, who accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch in a case against Qudamah ibn Maz'un; second, an analogy (qiyas): if a person has a limb cut off unjustly (like a hand), that does not impair 'adalah, so similarly, a eunuch whose testicles were removed unjustly remains 'adil. The commentary narrates the historical incident for context and emphasizes that the key is that the removal was unjust. If the eunuch voluntarily removed his testicles (e.g., self-mutilation), his testimony is rejected because that act is sinful and impairs 'adalah. The reasoning relies on the principle that unjust oppression does not diminish a person's legal reliability.

Key Terms
الخصى (al-khaṣī): A man who has been castrated; his testicles removed.
ظلما (ẓulman): Unjustly; through oppression or wrongdoing by another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is the testimony of a eunuch rejected according to this passage?
A) If he is a eunuch due to an accident
B) If he voluntarily removed his testicles
C) If he is also uncircumcised
D) If he is a eunuch and his hand is also cut

Key Takeaway
A eunuch's testimony is accepted unless he voluntarily castrated himself; unjust oppression does not affect legal reliability.

Testimony of a Child Born of Zina: Hanafi vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on testimony admissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of walad al-zina, explain the proof (a min al-awla and Quran 35:18), and distinguish the Maliki objection and Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A child's 'adalah is independent of the parents' sin: no soul bears another's burden.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: can a child born out of wedlock testify in a case of zina? The Hanafi school says yes, provided the child is 'adil (upright). Imam Malik disagreed, arguing such a child would be suspect. We'll examine each school's proof and see how Hanafi jurists refute the Maliki argument using the Quranic principle of individual responsibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the testimony of walad al-zina, including the key condition: the child must be 'adil.
The passage begins 'وَوَلَدُ الزِّنَا' — the matn states the ruling.
2
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the proof: a min al-awla argument from the parents' disbelief not disqualifying the child's testimony, and the direct Quranic evidence (35:18) that no one bears another's sin.
The commentary explains the logic: if kufr (greater sin) doesn't disqualify, then fisq (lesser sin) surely does not.
3
Identify the Maliki objection
State Imam Malik's position: the testimony of walad al-zina is rejected in zina cases because he would want others to be like him, making him suspect (mutaham).
The objection is based on the nature of human psychology, not on the child's actual character.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafi school rebuts the Maliki argument: the discussion is only about an 'adil person, who does not desire sin for others nor lie for that purpose.
This shifts the focus from status to actual character.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in Hanafi courts, the testimony is accepted if the child is known to be upright; in Maliki courts, it is automatically rejected in zina cases regardless of the child's character.
The dispute thus has real-world implications for litigants.

قال وولد الزناء لان فسق الابوين لا يوجب فسق الولد ككفرهما وهو مسلم وقال مالك لا تقبل في الزناء لانه يجب ان يكون غيره كمثله فيتهم قلنا العدل لا يختار ذالك ولا يستحبه والكلام فى العدل ترجمہ اور ولد الزنا کی گواہی بھی قبول ہوگی ۔ اس لئے کہ والدین کا فسق اولاد کے فسق کو واجب نہیں کرتا ہے۔ جیسے والدین کا کفر حالانکہ ولد مسلمان ہے اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ زنا کے مقدمہ میں ولد الزنا کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ وہ اس بات کو پسند کرے گا کہ اس کے علاوہ بھی اس کے مثل ہو تو وہ متہم ہوگا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ عادل آدمی جھوٹی گواہی اختیار نہیں کرے گا اور نہ اس کو پسند کرے گا ۔ اور گفتگو عادل میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ ولد الزنا کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کیونکہ زنا کا ارتکاب کرنے سے والدین فاسق ہوئے ہیں اور والدین کا فاسق ہونا ان کے کافر ہونے سے بڑھ کر نہیں ہے۔ اور والدین کا کافر ہونا مسلمان بیٹے کی شہادت سے مانع ہے۔ یعنی والدین کے کافر ہونے کے باوجود مسلمان بیٹے کی شہادت قبول کی جاتی ہے۔ پس والدین کے فاسق ہونے کی صورت میں بیٹے کی شہادت بدرجہ اولی قبول ہوگی۔ اس کی تائید باری تعالیٰ کے قول وَ لَا تَزِرُ وَازِرَةٌ وَزُرَ أُخرى سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ آیت کی روشنی میں والدین کا گناہ اولاد کے سر نہیں تھوپا جا سکتا ہے۔ حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ ولد الزنا کی گواہی زنا کے مقدمہ میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ اس بات کو پسند کرے گا کہ دوسرا بھی اس کے مثل ہو ۔ جیسا کہ مثل مشہور ہے کہ گبڑا یہ چاہتا ہے کہ ساری دنیا مجھ جیسی ہو جائے ۔ اور جب وہ اس بات کو پسند کرے گا تو وہ زنا کے مقدمہ میں اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہوگا اور متہم کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا اس کی گواہی زنا کے مقدمہ میں قبول نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ ہمارا کلام اس صورت میں ہے جب ولد الزنا عادل ہو اور عادل آدمی محض اس وجہ سے کہ دوسرا آدمی بھی مجھ جیسا ہو جائے ، جھوٹی گواہی اختیار نہیں کرے گا اور نہ دوسرے کی نسبت ایسا پسند کرے گا۔اور جب یہ بات ہے تو ولدالزناء اپنی گواہی میں متہم نہ ہوگا اور جب ولد الزنا اپنی گواہی میں متہم نہیں ہے تو اس کی گواہی قبول کرنے میں کیا مضائقہ ہے۔
He said: And the child of zina—because the sinfulness of the parents does not necessitate sinfulness of the child, just as their disbelief (does not make the child a disbeliever) while he is Muslim. And Malik said: It is not accepted in cases of zina because he would like that others be like him, so he is suspect. We say: The just person does not choose that nor desire it, and the discussion is about the just person. Translation: And the testimony of the child of zina is also accepted, because the parents' sin does not necessitate the child's sin, just as the parents' disbelief (does not make the child a disbeliever) while the child is Muslim. Imam Malik said: In a case of zina, the testimony of the child of zina is not accepted, because he would like that others be like him, so he is suspect. We say: A just person does not choose false testimony nor desire it, and the discussion is about the just person. Commentary: The author of al-Quduri stated that the testimony of a child of zina is accepted because the parents' commission of zina makes them sinful, and their sinfulness is not greater than their disbelief. And the parents' disbelief does not prevent the testimony of a Muslim son; i.e., despite the parents' disbelief, the testimony of a Muslim son is accepted. So even more so when the parents are sinful, the son's testimony is accepted. This is supported by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And no bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' (35:18). Because in the light of the verse, the parents' sin cannot be placed on the child. Imam Malik said that the testimony of a child of zina is not accepted in a case of zina, because he would like that another be like him, as the famous saying goes: 'the bastard wants the whole world to be like him.' And when he desires that, he is suspect in his testimony in a zina case, and the testimony of a suspect is not accepted. Therefore, his testimony in a zina case is not accepted. Our response is: Our discussion is in the case when the child of zina is just, and a just person will not choose false testimony merely so that another person becomes like him, nor will he desire that for others. And when that is the case, the child of zina is not suspect in his testimony, and when he is not suspect, there is no harm in accepting his testimony.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the testimony of a child born out of wedlock (walad al-zina). The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that his testimony is accepted in all cases, including charges of zina, because the parents' sin does not transmit to the child. The proof is a min al-awla (a fortiori) argument: if parents' disbelief does not disqualify a Muslim child's testimony, then their lesser sin (zina) certainly does not. This is reinforced by the Quranic principle that no soul bears another's burden (35:18). Imam Malik objects, arguing that in zina cases, a child of zina would naturally want others to be like him (to legitimize his birth), thus he is suspect (mutaham) and his testimony is rejected. The Hanafi response is that this argument only applies if the child is not 'adil (upright), but we are speaking of a just person who would not lie or desire sin for others. Therefore, if he is 'adil, his testimony is accepted. The resolution is that the child's character, not his birth, determines his reliability.

Key Terms
ولد الزنا (walad al-zinā): A child born from an illicit sexual relationship (zina).
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness; a state of being a fasiq (one who commits major sins or persists in minor sins).
متهم (mutaham): Suspect; one who has a personal interest in the outcome of a case, making his testimony unreliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because all children of zina are trustworthy
C) Because the Quran specifically orders it
D) Because Imam Malik agreed with them

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds individual legal responsibility: a child born of zina is not tainted by his parents' sin, and his testimony is accepted if he himself is just and upright.

Testimony of a Child Born of Fornication: Hanafi vs Maliki Dispute
Hanafi ruling contested by Malik, with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of walad al-zina, identify the Maliki objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the Qur'anic proof.

Core Idea
Fisq is not inherited; a just witness does not bear false testimony even if born of zina.

This lesson examines an inter-madhhab dispute about the testimony of a child born of fornication (walad al-zina). While the Hanafi school accepts such testimony unconditionally if the witness is 'adl, Imam Malik restricts it specifically in zina cases due to presumed bias. Understanding the Hanafi proof—grounded in individual responsibility and the presumption of 'adl—reveals a key difference in testimonial jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The passage begins by affirming that the testimony of walad al-zina is accepted. Note the core reasoning: the parents' fisq does not necessitate the child's fisq, analogous to a Muslim child of disbelieving parents whose testimony is accepted.
The analogy (qiyas) between fisq and kufr is central to the Hanafi argument.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik is cited as holding that walad al-zina's testimony is not accepted in cases of zina. The basis is tuhma (accusation of bias): he might desire others to be like him, compromising his objectivity.
The dispute is limited to zina cases; Malik may accept it in other cases.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik's reasoning: a walad al-zina may prefer that others share his condition, leading to false testimony to implicate the accused. The commentary cites a proverb: 'The bastard wants everyone to be like him.' This tuhma disqualifies him in zina cases.
This is a psychological objection based on possible motive, not on parentage alone.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: 'Our discussion is when the walad al-zina is 'adl.' A just person does not choose false testimony nor desire others to be like him in sin. Thus, tuhma is removed. The Quranic verse 6:164 (no bearer of burdens bears another's burden) is invoked to reject inherited sin.
The response reframes the debate: the ruling applies only to an 'adl witness.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi practice, walad al-zina's testimony is admissible without restriction if he is proven 'adl. In Maliki practice, his testimony is inadmissible specifically in zina cases, regardless of his 'adl. This difference affects litigation involving zina accusations.
The Hanafi position is more permissive, relying on individual character rather than background.

He said: And the testimony of a child born of fornication (is accepted) because the sinfulness (fisq) of the parents does not necessitate the sinfulness of the child, just like their disbelief while the child is Muslim. Malik said: It is not accepted in (cases of) fornication because he would wish that others be like him, so he is accused. We said: The just person does not choose that nor desire it, and the discussion is about the just person. Translation: And the testimony of a child born of fornication will also be accepted because the sinfulness of the parents does not necessitate the sinfulness of the child, just like the parents' disbelief while the child is Muslim. Imam Malik said that in a case of fornication, the testimony of a child born of fornication will not be accepted because he would desire that others be like him, so he becomes accused. We say that a just person does not choose false testimony nor desires it, and the discussion concerns the just person. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri stated that the testimony of a child born of fornication will not be accepted because committing fornication makes the parents sinful, and the parents' being sinful is not greater than their being disbelievers. And the parents' disbelief does not prevent the Muslim son's testimony, i.e., despite the parents' disbelief, the Muslim son's testimony is accepted. So in the case of the parents' sinfulness, the son's testimony is a fortiori accepted. This is supported by Allah's statement: 'And no bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' (Quran 6:164), because in light of the verse, the parents' sin cannot be placed on the child. Imam Malik said the testimony of a child born of fornication is not accepted in a fornication case because he would desire that another be like him, as the famous proverb says: 'The bastard wants everyone to be like him.' And when he desires that, he becomes accused in his testimony in a fornication case, and the testimony of an accused person is not accepted. So his testimony in a fornication case will not be accepted. Our response is that our discussion is when the child born of fornication is just ('adl), and a just person does not give false testimony merely because another person becomes like him, nor does he desire that for others. And when this is the case, the child born of fornication will not be accused in his testimony, and when he is not accused, what harm is there in accepting his testimony?
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a child born of fornication (walad al-zina), along with a dispute with Imam Malik. The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author first states the Hanafi position: the testimony of such a person is accepted. The reasoning is that the parents' sin (fisq) does not transfer to the child, just as the parents' disbelief does not make the child a disbeliever if he is Muslim. The Qur'anic verse 'No bearer of burdens bears the burden of another' (6:164) is cited in support, establishing individual responsibility. Imam Malik's objection is then presented: in a case of fornication (zina), the walad al-zina might desire that others be like him (i.e., also born of fornication), which would make him biased (mutaham) and thus his testimony should be rejected, especially in a zina case. The Hanafi response counters that this discussion assumes the walad al-zina is just ('adl). A just person does not give false testimony merely out of a desire for others to be like him; indeed, he does not even desire that. Thus, the accusation of bias is removed. The Hanafi position is upheld: his testimony is accepted, even in zina cases, provided he is just. Quduri's objection (that the testimony is not accepted at all) is noted but overridden by the stronger Hanafi reasoning. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that fisq is individual and not inherited, and that 'adl (justness) is the primary criterion for testimonial acceptance.

Key Terms
ولد الزنا (walad al-zinā): A child born from an unlawful sexual relationship (fornication).
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness or immoral conduct, specifically sin that disqualifies a person from being 'adl (just) in testimony.
عدل ('adl): A just person whose testimony is accepted; one who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and maintains upright character.
تہمہ (tuhma): Accusation of bias or suspicion that a witness might lie due to personal interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the testimony of a child born of fornication if he is 'adl, relying on individual responsibility and rejecting inherited sin.

Testimony of a Hermaphrodite: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on accepting testimony of a hermaphrodite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a hermaphrodite and apply the precautionary rule for covering gender ambiguity.

Core Idea
A hermaphrodite's testimony is valid except in hadd and qisas, with a precaution to pair with a man and a woman.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the testimony of a khuntha (hermaphrodite). While gender ambiguity might seem to disqualify a witness, the school accepts it based on the Quranic principle of two men or a man and two women. The ruling balances inclusion with caution, especially in serious cases like hudud and qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'Shahadat al-khuntha ja'izah' — the testimony of a hermaphrodite is permissible.
2
Understand the reason
Because a khuntha is either male or female, and the testimony of both genders is accepted in principle based on Quran 2:282.
3
Note the condition
The khuntha must be 'adl (just). Without this, testimony is not accepted.
4
Apply the precaution (ihtiyat)
It is recommended for the khuntha to testify alongside one man and one woman to cover both gender possibilities.
If the khuntha is female, this yields one man and two women (minimum for financial cases). If male, it yields two men and one woman (exceeds minimum).
5
Recognize the exception
The testimony of a khuntha is not accepted in hadd (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) cases, because women's testimony is not accepted in those categories, and the khuntha might be a woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وشهادة الخنثى جائزة لانه رجل أو امرأة وشهادة الجنسين مقبولة با ترجمہ اور خنثی کی گواہی جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ مرد ہے یا عورت ہے اور نص کی رو سے دونوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ تشریح خشی وہ ہے جس کے اندر مرد و عورت دونوں کی علامت پیدائشی ہو۔ پس اگر منشی عادل ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ مرد ہو گا یا عورت ہوگی اور قرآن سے ثابت ہے کہ دونوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے و استشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان - احتیاط یہ ہے کہ خشی کے ساتھ ایک مرد اور ایک عورت گواہی دے۔ کیونکہ خفشی اگر عورت ہوگی تو اس صورت میں ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہ ہوں گی۔ اور اگر خشی مرد ہے تو اس صورت میں دو مرد گواہ ہوں گے اور عورت زائد ہوگی ۔ اور یہ بھی مناسب ہے کہ حدود و قصاص میں منشی کی گواہی قبول نہ کی جائے کیونکہ خنثی میں عورت ہونے کا بھی احتمال ہے حالانکہ حدود و قصاص میں عورتوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی۔
He said: And the testimony of a hermaphrodite (khuntha) is permissible because he is either a man or a woman, and the testimony of both genders is accepted. Translation: And the testimony of a hermaphrodite is permissible because he is either a man or a woman, and according to the text, the testimony of both is accepted. Explanation: A khuntha is one who has both male and female signs at birth. So if the khuntha is just ('adl), his testimony will be accepted because he will be either a man or a woman, and it is established from the Quran that the testimony of both is accepted. Indeed, Allah says: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men. And if there are not two men, then a man and two women.' (2:282) Precaution is that the khuntha should testify along with one man and one woman. Because if the khuntha is a woman, then in that case there will be one man and two women witnesses. And if the khuntha is a man, then in that case there will be two men witnesses and an additional woman. And it is also appropriate that the testimony of a khuntha should not be accepted in cases of hadd and qisas because the khuntha may also be a woman, whereas in hadd and qisas, the testimony of women is not accepted.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the testimony of a hermaphrodite (khuntha). The passage type is a definition-ruling, as it first defines khuntha then states the ruling. The author states that the testimony of a khuntha is permissible (ja'iz) because a khuntha is either male or female, and the testimony of both genders is accepted in principle, based on the Quranic verse (2:282) which mentions two men or a man and two women. The key condition is that the khuntha must be 'adl (just). The text then offers a practical precaution (ihtiyat): when a khuntha testifies, it is better for him/her to do so alongside one man and one woman. This covers both possibilities: if the khuntha is female, then there would be one man and two women (which is the required minimum for financial cases); if the khuntha is male, then there would be two men and one extra woman (which exceeds the requirement). The author also notes that it is appropriate (munaasib) not to accept the testimony of a khuntha in hadd (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) cases, because women's testimony is not accepted in those categories, and the khuntha might be a woman. Thus, to avoid doubt, the testimony of a khuntha is excluded from such cases. This aligns with the Hanafi principle of preferring caution in matters where gender ambiguity exists.

Key Terms
خنثی (khunthā): A person born with both male and female genitalia or ambiguous physical signs; a hermaphrodite.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony given in court; a legally binding statement by witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school recommend that a hermaphrodite (khuntha) testify alongside one man and one woman?
A) To ensure the number of witnesses exceeds the minimum requirement.
B) To cover the possibility that the khuntha may be either male or female, thus always meeting the required witness composition.
C) Because the Quran explicitly requires that specific combination.
D) To avoid confusion about the khuntha's gender in court.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the testimony of a hermaphrodite as valid in financial cases, excludes it from hadd and qisas, and recommends a precautionary pairing to cover gender ambiguity.

Testimony of Government Officials
Ruling on acceptance of testimony by state officials

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on the testimony of government officials, identify the condition that disqualifies them, and explain the exception when they possess wajahah and muruwwa.

Core Idea
A government official's testimony is valid by default; only assistance in injustice disqualifies, but status and dignity can remove suspicion.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition addresses a common question: can government officials serve as witnesses? The default answer is yes. However, when officials assist in injustice, their credibility is compromised. Building on a ruling from Imam Abu Yusuf, the passage also presents a nuanced exception: if the official has high status and personal dignity, his testimony may still be accepted, because such qualities make false testimony unlikely. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate how the Hanafi school weighs social factors in assessing witness integrity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage begins by stating that the testimony of officials (al-ummal) is ja'iz (permissible). This is the default ruling. Note that the term 'officials' is specified as those appointed by the sultan.
The default acceptance is based on the principle that the position itself is not sin (fisq).
2
Determine the condition that changes the ruling
The default ruling applies only if the official does not assist in injustice (zulm). If they do assist in injustice, their 'adala (justness) falls and their testimony is rejected.
Assisting injustice is considered fisq, which directly impacts witness credibility.
3
Explore the exception based on status and dignity
Some scholars, building on Abu Yusuf's view, hold that even an official who helps in injustice may still testify if he is wajih (of high status) and possesses muruwwa (dignity). The rationale is that such a person would not risk his reputation by lying, and others would not dare hire him for false testimony.
This exception removes the suspicion (tuhma) of dishonesty, a key concept in Hanafi witness law.
4
Understand the underlying rationale
The acceptance hinges on the removal of tuhma. Wajahah and muruwwa make lying unlikely, restoring the presumption of truthfulness. The passage cites the practice of the Companions who served as officials, confirming that the position itself does not disqualify.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on contextual factors when assessing 'adala.

He said: And the testimony of officials (al-ummal) is permissible, and what is meant is the officials of the sultan according to the general body of scholars (ammat al-mashayikh), because the action itself is not sin (fisq) unless they are helpers in injustice. And it was said: If the official is of high status (wajih) among the people, possessing dignity (muruwwa), does not speak recklessly, his testimony is accepted, as has passed from Abu Yusuf concerning the sinful person (al-fasiq). Because due to his status, he does not proceed to lying in order to preserve his dignity, and due to his awe (haybah), he is not hired for false testimony. Translation: And the testimony of officials is permissible, and according to the general body of scholars, what is meant is the officials of the sultan, because the action itself is not sin unless these people are helpers in injustice. And it was said: If the official is of high status and dignified among the people, and does not speak recklessly, then his testimony will be accepted, as has passed from Abu Yusuf concerning the sinful person. Because due to his status, he will not proceed to lying in order to preserve his dignity, and due to his awe, he cannot be hired for false testimony. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the testimony of officials is permissible, and by officials is meant those officials of the sultan who assist in collecting obligatory dues, like those who collect kharaj and zakah of grazing animals (sawa'im), because the action itself is not sin. And being an official is not sin because many great Companions were officials. Yes, if the officials of the sultan help the king in injustice, as in our times they assist the sultan in injustice, then their testimony will not be accepted, because by helping in injustice, their justness ('adala) has fallen. Some scholars have said: If an official helps in injustice but is of high status and dignified among the people, and does not speak recklessly, then his testimony is also accepted, as has passed from Imam Abu Yusuf concerning the sinful person: if the sinful person is of high status and dignified, his testimony is accepted. Because the official who helps in injustice, due to his status, will not proceed to lying in order to preserve his dignity, and due to his awe, cannot be hired or paid for false testimony. So when the suspicion of lying is removed due to status and awe, the testimony (is accepted).
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the testimony of government officials (ummal). The passage type is a ruling statement. The author begins by stating that the testimony of officials is permissible (ja'iz), clarifying that by 'officials' is meant the sultan's tax collectors and administrators, as per the general body of scholars. The reason is that the mere act of being an official is not sin (fisq); many Companions held such posts. However, if these officials assist in injustice (zulm), then their justness is compromised and their testimony becomes unacceptable. The passage then presents a nuanced view from some scholars, building on Imam Abu Yusuf's earlier ruling about the sinful person (fasiq): if an official, even one who assists in injustice, possesses high social status (wajahah) and personal dignity (muruwwa), and does not speak frivolously, his testimony may still be accepted. The rationale is that his status deters him from lying (he values his reputation), and his awe inhibits others from hiring him for false testimony. Thus, when the suspicion (tuhma) of lying is removed, the testimony is accepted. This illustrates an important Hanafi principle: the default assumption of 'adala (justness) can be restored or retained if countervailing factors (like status and dignity) eliminate the likelihood of dishonesty. The passage also references the Companions' involvement in official duties as evidence that the position itself is not disqualifying.

Key Terms
عمال (ʿummāl): Government officials, specifically those appointed by the sultan to collect taxes and administer duties.
مروة (murūwa): Personal dignity, chivalry, and social reputation that prevents a person from engaging in base acts like lying.
وجاهة (wajāhah): High social status and respect among people, which deters the person from dishonesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The default ruling is that testimony of government officials is valid; only assisting injustice disqualifies, but even then, status and dignity can remove suspicion and restore acceptance.

Testimony of a Hermaphrodite (Khuntha) is Valid
Ruling with Quranic proof and precaution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a khuntha, derive the proof from Quran 2:282, and apply the exception for hudud and qisas.

Core Idea
Khuntha's testimony is valid because scripture accepts both male and female witnesses.

The Hanafi school addresses the legal status of a person born with ambiguous gender signs. This lesson examines the validity of their testimony in court, grounding the ruling in the Quranic verse on witnessing. We will also explore a practical precaution and a key exception for hudud and qisas cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first line: 'And the testimony of the hermaphrodite is permissible.' What is the act being ruled upon? The act of giving testimony (shahadah) by a khuntha. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) if the khuntha is just ('adil).
The khuntha must be morally upright; justice is a condition for any witness.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 2:282: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men, and if there are not two men, then a man and two women.' This is the primary evidence. Identify the text category: it is a command (amr) indicating permissibility/obligation of accepting certain configurations.
The dalil is Quranic, qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah in this context because it's interpreted for the khuntha.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the khuntha's validity? The verse accepts witnesses who are either men or women. A khuntha is either male or female, so his/her testimony falls under one of the permitted categories. The wajh al-dalalah is the inclusive disjunction: the khuntha's testimony is covered by either 'men' or 'women'.
The ruling relies on the principle that the khuntha's true gender is hidden but must be one of the two.
4
Note the precaution and exception
The author adds a caution: it is recommended to have an extra man or woman with the khuntha to ensure the correct count. Also, in hudud and qisas, the khuntha's testimony is not accepted because of the possibility of being female (women's testimony is not accepted in those cases). This is an extension based on caution (ihtiyat) and the principle of avoiding doubt (shubha).
This is part of the Hanafi position, not a dispute with other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
خنثی کی گواہی کا حکم
قال وشهادة الخنثى جائزة لانه رجل أو امرأة وشهادة الجنسين مقبولة با
ترجمہ اور خنثی کی گواہی جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ مرد ہے یا عورت ہے اور نص کی رو سے دونوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ تشریح خشی وہ ہے جس کے اندر مرد و عورت دونوں کی علامت پیدائشی ہو۔ پس اگر منشی عادل ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ مرد ہو گا یا عورت ہوگی اور قرآن سے ثابت ہے کہ دونوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے و استشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان - احتیاط یہ ہے کہ خشی کے ساتھ ایک مرد اور ایک عورت گواہی دے۔ کیونکہ خفشی اگر عورت ہوگی تو اس صورت میں ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہ ہوں گی۔ اور اگر خشی مرد ہے تو اس صورت میں دو مرد گواہ ہوں گے اور عورت زائد ہوگی ۔ اور یہ بھی مناسب ہے کہ حدود و قصاص میں منشی کی گواہی قبول نہ کی جائے کیونکہ خنثی میں عورت ہونے کا بھی احتمال ہے حالانکہ حدود و قصاص میں عورتوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی۔
And the testimony of the hermaphrodite is permissible because he is a man or a woman, and the testimony of both sexes is accepted by the text. Translation: And the testimony of the hermaphrodite is permissible because he is a man or a woman, and the testimony of both sexes is accepted according to the text. Explanation: Khuntha is one who has both male and female signs at birth. So if the khuntha is just ('adil), his testimony will be accepted, because he will be either a man or a woman, and it is proven from the Quran that the testimony of both is accepted. Thus the command: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men, and if there are not two men, then a man and two women.' Caution: It is recommended that a man and a woman testify along with the khuntha. Because if the khuntha is a woman, then in that case there will be one man and two women. And if the khuntha is a man, then there will be two men and a woman extra. And it is also appropriate that in hudud and qisas the testimony of the khuntha should not be accepted, because there is a possibility of the khuntha being a woman, while the testimony of women is not accepted in hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the testimony of a khuntha (hermaphrodite). The author states that the testimony of a khuntha is valid because they are either male or female, and the testimony of both genders is accepted in Islamic law. The proof is from the Quran (2:282) which commands two male witnesses or one male and two females. The khuntha must be 'adil (just). However, as a precaution, it is recommended to have an additional male or female witness alongside the khuntha to ensure the required number of witnesses regardless of the khuntha's gender. Additionally, in cases of hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation), the testimony of a khuntha is not accepted because there is a possibility that the khuntha is female, and women's testimony is not accepted in these cases. This is based on the principle of caution.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A person who has both male and female reproductive signs at birth.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court; evidence.
عادل ('adil): Just; morally upright person whose testimony is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because khuntha is always considered female
B) Because khuntha is never considered just
C) Because there is a possibility the khuntha is female, and women's testimony is not accepted in those cases
D) Because khuntha are not allowed to testify in any case

Key Takeaway
A khuntha's testimony is generally valid if they are just, but is rejected in hudud and qisas due to the possibility of being female.

Testimony of Government Officials (Ummal) – Default and Exceptional Conditions
Ruling on testimony of government workers with conditional exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of government officials and apply the conditions that can lead to its acceptance or rejection.

Core Idea
Government officials' testimony is accepted unless they help in oppression, but even then respect and manliness may restore acceptance.

This passage addresses a practical question: can the testimony of a government worker ('amil) be accepted in court? The default ruling is that it is permissible, as the job itself is not sinful—many Companions held such posts. However, if the official assists the ruler in oppression (zulm), his 'adalah (justness) is compromised. Yet, following Imam Abu Yusuf, some Hanafi scholars allow acceptance if the official possesses respect (wajaha) and manliness (muru'ah), as these qualities make false testimony unlikely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Find the phrase that states the ruling on testimony of government officials and note its legal category (jā'iz).
2
Locate the exception
Identify the condition that causes rejection: when the official is a helper in oppression. Understand why this compromises 'adalah.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi expansion
Notice the additional opinion (from Imam Abu Yusuf) that even a helper can be accepted if he has wajaha and muru'ah. Understand the rationale: these qualities remove the suspicion of lying.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; some scholars accept this view, others reject unconditionally.
4
Apply the conditions
Given a scenario, determine whether the official's testimony would be accepted by checking: (1) does he help in oppression? (2) if yes, does he have respect and manliness?

قال وشهادة العمال جائزة والمراد عُمّال السلطان عند عامة المشائخ لان نفس العمل ليس بفسق الا اذا كانوا اعوانا على الظلم وقيل العامل اذا كان وجيها فى الناس ذا مروّة لا يجازف فى كلامه تقبل شهادته كما مر عن ابي يوسف فى الفاسق لانه لو جاهته لا يُقدم على الكذب حفظا للمروة ولمهابته لا يستاجر على الشهادة الكاذبة
ترجمہ اور عمال کی گواہی جائز ہے اور عامتہ المشائخ کے نزدیک سلطان کے شمال مراد ہیں۔ کیونکہ نفس عمل فسق نہیں ہے مگر جب یہ لوگ ظلم پر مددگار ہوں اور کہا گیا کہ عامل جب لوگوں میں وجیہ صاحب مروت ہو ، اپنے کلام میں بے ہودہ گو نہ ہو، تو اس کی شہادت قبول ہوگی ۔ جیسا کہ فاسق کے بارے میں ابو یوسف سے گزر چکا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ اپنی وجاہت کی وجہ سے جھوٹ پر اقدام نہیں کرے گا تا کہ
اس کی مروت محفوظ رہے اور اپنی ہیبت کی وجہ سے جھوٹی گواہی پر اجرت پر نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ تشریح . صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ عمال کی گواہنی جائز ہے اور عمال سے سلطان کے وہ عمال مراد ہیں جو حقوق واجبہ وصول کرنے میں سلطان کی مدد کرتے ہیں۔ جیسے خراج اور سوائم کی زکوۃ وصول کرنے والے حضرات کیونکہ خود عمل کوئی فسق نہیں۔ اور عامل ہو نا فسق اس لئے نہیں کہ بڑے بڑے صحابہ عمال تھے ۔ ہاں اگر عمال سلطان بادشاہ کے ظلم پر مددگار ہوں جیسے آج کل سلطان کے ظلم پر سلطان کی مدد کرتے ہیں تو ان کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ظلم پر مدد کرنے کی وجہ سے ان کی عدالت ساقط ہوگئی ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ عامل اگر ظلم پر مددگار ہومگر لوگوں میں باوجاہت اور با مروت ہو۔ اور بے تکی اور بے ہودہ باتیں نہ کرتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول کر لی جائے گی ۔ جیسا کہ امام ابو یوسف سے فاسق کے سلسلہ میں گزر چکا ہے کہ فاسق اگر باوجاہت اور بامروت ہوتو اس کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ ظلم پر مدد کرنے والا عامل اپنی وجاہت کی وجہ سے جھوٹ بولنے پر اقدام نہیں کرے گا تا کہ اس کی مروت محفوظ رہے اور اپنی ہیبت کی وجہ سے جھوٹی گواہی پر اجیر اور مزدور نہیں بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس جب وجاہت اور ہیبت کی وجہ سے جھوٹ کی تہمت ختم ہو گئی تو گواہی
قبول کرنے میں کیا مضائقہ ہے۔
And the testimony of workers (government officials) is permissible, and by 'workers' is meant the officials of the sultan according to the majority of scholars, because the work itself is not sinful unless they are helpers in oppression. And it is said: when the worker is respected among people, having manliness (muru'ah), not using vain speech, his testimony is accepted, as has passed from Abu Yusuf regarding the sinful person (fasiq), because his respect prevents him from lying to preserve his manliness, and due to his awe he cannot be hired for false testimony. Translation: And the testimony of government officials is permissible, and according to the generality of the scholars, they mean the officials of the sultan, because the work itself is not sinful except when they are helpers in oppression. And it is said that when an official is respected and has manliness, and does not speak nonsense, his testimony will be accepted, as has passed from Abu Yusuf regarding the sinful person, because due to his respect he will not commit lying to preserve his manliness, and due to his awe he will not be hired for false testimony. Explanation: The author of al-Quduri said that the testimony of officials is permissible, and by officials are meant those who help the sultan in collecting obligatory rights, like those who collect kharaj and zakat on grazing animals, because the work itself is not sinful, and being an official is not sin because many great Companions were officials. However, if the officials help the sultan in oppression, like today they help the sultan in oppression, their testimony will not be accepted because their 'adalah (justness) is lost due to helping in oppression. Some scholars said that if an official helps in oppression but is respected and has manliness, and does not speak vainly, his testimony will also be accepted, as passed from Imam Abu Yusuf regarding a sinful person that if he is respected and has manliness, his testimony will be accepted, because the helper in oppression will not commit lying due to his respect to preserve his manliness, and due to his awe he cannot be hired for false testimony. So when the accusation of falsehood is removed due to respect and awe, what harm is there in accepting his testimony?
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage deals with the testimony of government officials (sing. 'amil, pl. 'ummal). The default ruling is that their testimony is accepted, as the act of being an official is not inherently sinful. The great Companions held such positions. However, if they are involved in helping the ruler in oppression (zulm), their 'adalah is compromised and their testimony is rejected. Some scholars follow the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf that even a sinful person (fasiq) can have his testimony accepted if he is a person of respect (wajaha) and manliness (muru'ah), as such a person is unlikely to lie. This is because he values his reputation and cannot be bribed. Thus, even an official who assists in oppression may have his testimony accepted if he possesses these qualities, as the reason for rejection (the accusation of falsehood) is removed.

Key Terms
عمال (ummal): Government officials who collect taxes and dues under the sultan.
وجاہت (wajaha): Social respect, high standing among people.
مروت (muru'ah): Manliness, dignity, sense of honor that prevents base actions.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness, departure from obedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When he is any government employee
B) When he helps the sultan in oppression and lacks respect and manliness
C) When he is a known sinner (fasiq)
D) When his work involves collecting taxes

Key Takeaway
A government official's testimony is default accepted; only assisting in oppression without redeeming social qualities leads to rejection, but even then, respect and manliness can restore acceptance.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony of Sons About Father's Appointment of Executor
Ruling on acceptance of testimony when executor claims appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony of interested parties about appointment of an executor and explain the qiyas vs istihsan reasoning.

Core Idea
Testimony of sons is accepted if the executor claims it, because istihsan overrides qiyas.

This passage presents a nuanced ruling in testimony law. While qiyas would reject any testimony where the witness stands to benefit, the Hanafi school applies istihsan to accept such testimony when it merely helps the judge identify the appointed executor. We will analyze the cases and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
The passage lists several scenarios: sons, legatees, creditors, debtors, co-executors testifying about appointment of executor. The ruling: accepted by istihsan if the executor claims it, denied if he denies.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Qiyas says such testimony is not accepted because the witness benefits (عود المنفعة). This is the general principle that self-serving testimony is rejected.
Standard Hanafi rule: testimony with direct benefit to witness is rejected by qiyas.
3
Examine the istihsan basis
Istihsan says the judge has authority to appoint an executor when death is known and someone claims it. The testimony merely assists the judge in identifying the appointee, similar to drawing lots, so it is accepted.
The judge's authority is key: he can appoint even without testimony, so testimony only helps identify.
4
Apply the distinction to different parties
The passage extends to legatees, creditors, debtors, and co-executors. In each case, if the testimony benefits the witness, qiyas rejects, but istihsan accepts based on the judge's authority. Exception: if death is unknown, the judge cannot appoint, so testimony must establish death itself; debtors' testimony establishes their own debt and thus death.
For debtors, testimony accepted even if death unknown because they confess a debt against themselves.
5
Note the practical difference
The mufta bihi position is the istihsan ruling. This is a clear example of how Hanafi jurisprudence gives weight to practical considerations over strict analogy.
Tarjih authority: the explicit text 'jā'iz istihsānan' indicates preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا شهد الرجلان ان اباهما اوصى الى فلان والوصى يدعى ذالك فهو جائز استحسانا وان انكر الوصى لم يجز وفى القياس لا يجوز وان ادعى وعلى هذا اذا شهد الموصى لهما بذالك او غریمان لهما على الميت دين او للميت عليهما دين وشهد الوصيان انه اوصى الى هذا الرجل معهما وجه القياس انها شهادة للشاهد لعود المنفعة اليه وجه الاستحسان للقاضى ولاية نصب الوصى اذا كان طالبا والموت معروفا فيكفى القاضى بهذه الشهادة مؤنة التعيين لا أن يثبت بها شيء فصار كالقرعة والوصيان اذا اقرا ان معهما ثالثا يملك القاضی نصب ثالث معهما لعجزهما عن التصرف باعترافهما بخلاف ما اذا انكر أو لم يُعرف الموت لانه ليس له ولاية نصب الوصى فتكون الشهادة هى الموجبة وفي الغريمين للميت عليهما دين تقبل الشهادة وان لم يكن الموت معروفا لانهما يقران على انفسهما فيثبت الموت افهم ـا فى حقهمـ
باعت
ترجمہ اور اگر دو مردوں نے گواہی دی کہ ان کے باپ نے فلان شخص کو وصی مقرر کیا ہے اور وصی بھی اس کا مدعی ہے تو یہ استحسانا جائز ہے اور اگر وصی منکر ہو تو جائز نہیں ہے اور قیاس میں جائز نہیں اگر چہ مدعی ہو اور اسی پر اگر دو شخصوں نے جن کے واسطے وصیت کی گئی اس کی گواہی دی یا دو قرض خواہوں نے جن کا میت پر قرضہ ہے یا جن پر میت کا قرضہ ہے یا دو ھیوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ میت نے اس شخص کو ہم دونوں کے ساتھ وصی بنایا ہے قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ گواہی خود گواہ کے واسطے ہے کیونکہ اس گواہی کی منفعت خود گواہ کو پہنچتی ہے۔ اور استحیان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی کو وصی مقرر کرنے کا خود اختیار ہے جبکہ اس کا طالب ہو۔ اور موت معروف ہو۔ پس قاضی اس شہادت کی وجہ سے تعیین کی تکلیف سے کفایت کرے گا۔ یہ نہیں کہ اس گواہی کی وجہ سے کوئی چیز ثابت کی جائے گی ۔ پس یہ قرعہ کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور دونوں وصیوں نے جب یہ اقرار کر لیا کہ دونوں کے ساتھ ایک تیسرا وصی ہے تو قاضی ان دونوں کیسا تھ ایک تیسرا وصی مقرر کرنے کا مالک ہوگا کیونکہ یہ دونوں اپنے اقرار کی وجہ سے تصرف کرنے سے عاجز ہیں۔ برخلاف اس کے جب وصی نے انکار کیا یا موت معروف نہ ہو اس لئے کہ قاضی کو وصی مقرر کرنے کی ولایت نہیں ہے۔ پس یہی گواہی موجب ہوگی۔ اور دونوں قرضداروں کی صورت میں جن پر میت کا قرضہ ہے گواہی قبول ہو جائے گی اگر چہ موت معروف نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں اپنی ذات پر قرضہ کا اقرار کرتے ہیں۔ پس ان دونوں کے حق میں ان دونوں کے اعتراف سے موت ثابت ہو جائیگی۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں پانچ مسئلے مذکور ہیں
ا دو مردوں نے یہ گواہ دی کہ ہمارے مرحوم باپ نے حامد کو وصی مقرر کیا ہے اور وصی یعنی حامد بھی اس کا مدعی ہے۔ - دو شخصوں نے جن کے واسطے مال کی وصیت کی گئی ہے یہ گواہی دی کہ فلاں مرحوم نے حامد کو اپنا وصی مقرر کیا ہے اور حامد بھی اپنے وصی
And if two men testify that their father appointed so-and-so as executor and the executor claims that, then it is valid by istihsan. But if the executor denies it, it is not valid. And by qiyas it is not valid even if he claims. And similarly if the two legatees (those for whom wasiyya was made) testify to that, or two creditors who have a debt against the deceased, or two debtors who owe the deceased a debt, or two executors testify that he appointed this man along with them. The basis of qiyas is that this testimony is for the witness because benefit returns to him. The basis of istihsan is that the judge has authority to appoint an executor when he is a claimant and the death is known. So the judge is saved by this testimony from the trouble of appointment (ta'yin), not that something is established by it, so it becomes like a lottery. And when the two executors confess that there is a third with them, the judge has the authority to appoint a third with them because they are incapable of acting due to their confession. Unlike if he denies or death is not known, because the judge has no authority to appoint an executor, so the testimony itself is the cause of establishment. And in the case of two debtors who owe a debt to the deceased, the testimony is accepted even if death is not known, because they confess against themselves, so death is established in their favor. Translation: ... (Urdu commentary follows)... Explanation: In this expression, five issues are mentioned: 1. Two men testify that their deceased father appointed Hamid as executor, and the executor Hamid claims that... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage deals with a complex scenario where two men testify that their father appointed a particular person as executor (wasi). The ruling is that if the executor himself claims the appointment, their testimony is accepted by istihsan, but if he denies it, it is not accepted. By qiyas, the testimony would not be accepted even if he claims, because the witnesses (the sons) benefit from the testimony (they are interested parties). However, istihsan is preferred because the judge has the authority to appoint an executor when requested, and the testimony merely helps the judge identify the appointee, similar to drawing lots (qur'ah). The passage also covers analogous cases: legatees, creditors, debtors, and co-executors testifying about the appointment. In each case, the principle is that if the testimony is self-serving (benefit to the witness), qiyas rejects it, but istihsan accepts it because it only facilitates the judge's appointment authority. Special cases: if the executor confesses that there is a third executor, the judge can appoint a third because the two are incapacitated by their own admission. If death is not known, the judge cannot appoint, so the testimony must establish the fact itself. In the case of debtors, their testimony is accepted even without known death because they confess a debt, establishing death in their favor.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): Executor appointed by a person to carry out their will after death.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas due to a stronger consideration.
عود المنفعة (awd al-manfa'ah): Return of benefit: when the witness stands to gain from the testimony, this disqualifies them by qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When the executor claims the appointment
C) When the sons are also beneficiaries
D) When death is unknown

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts self-serving testimony in executor appointment by istihsan because the judge's authority to appoint makes the testimony merely assist identification, not establish a right.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony on Appointment of Executor: Between Qiyas and Istihsan
Ruling with reasoning on acceptance of testimony when beneficiaries also claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts testimony that appears self-beneficial using istihsan, and contrast this with the qiyas argument of other schools.

Core Idea
When the judge can appoint an executor himself, testimony merely assists identification—benefit does not invalidate.

Consider a scenario: two sons testify that their father appointed a certain person as executor. The sons stand to benefit because the executor will manage the estate. Should their testimony be accepted? The majority of jurists say no, by analogy to the rule against self-interested testimony. But the Hanafi school says yes, by istihsan, because the judge has independent authority to appoint an executor. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Basic Scenario
Read the first line of the source: two sons testify that their father appointed an executor, and the executor confirms. The Hanafi ruling is 'ja'iz istihsanan' (permissible by juridical preference). Note the key condition: the executor must also claim the appointment.
If the executor denies, the testimony is rejected because the judge cannot appoint an unwilling person.
2
Understand the Qiyas Argument
The text states 'fi al-qiyas la yajuz wa in idda'a' (by qiyas it is not permissible even if he claims). The opposing argument is that the sons benefit from the appointment (e.g., having an executor manage the estate), so their testimony is biased and rejected. This is the default rule for testimony with self-interest.
This qiyas is based on the principle that testimony for one's own benefit is presumptively unreliable.
3
Grasp the Istihsan Exception
The Hanafi istihsan reasoning: the judge has the authority (wilaya) to appoint an executor if the death is known (ma'ruf) and a willing person exists. The testimony merely helps the judge identify the candidate; it does not establish the appointment itself. Hence, the tuhma (suspicion of bias) does not apply. The analogy to lottery (qur'a) illustrates that the testimony is just a selection tool.
The condition of known death is critical. If death is not known, the judge lacks authority, and the testimony becomes the basis, which is invalid.
4
Examine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis accept such testimony in court, so the executor can be confirmed without additional evidence. Other schools reject it, requiring alternative proof or judicial appointment from scratch.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, as it is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by Imam Muhammad's texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: وإذا شهد الرجلان أن أباهما أوصى إلى فلان والوصي يدّعي ذلك فهو جائز استحسانا، وإن أنكر الوصي لم يجز، وفي القياس لا يجوز وإن ادعى. وعلى هذا إذا شهد الموصى لهما بذلك، أو غريمان لهما على الميت دين، أو للميت عليهما دين، وشهد الوصيان أنه أوصى إلى هذا الرجل معهما. وجه القياس: أنها شهادة للشاهد لعود المنفعة إليه. وجه الاستحسان: للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصي إذا كان طالبا والموت معروفا، فيكفي القاضي بهذه الشهادة مؤنة التعيين لا أن يثبت بها شيء، فصار كالقرعة. والوصيان إذا أقرا أن معهما ثالثا يملك القاضي نصب ثالث معهما لعجزهما عن التصرف باعترافهما، بخلاف ما إذا أنكر أو لم يُعرف الموت، لأنه ليس له ولاية نصب الوصي فتكون الشهادة هي الموجبة. وفي الغريمين للميت عليهما دين تقبل الشهادة وإن لم يكن الموت معروفا، لأنهما يقران على أنفسهما فيثبت الموت في حقهما.
He said: When two men testify that their father appointed so-and-so as executor and the executor claims that, it is permissible by istihsan; if the executor denies, it is not permissible. By qiyas, it is not permissible even if he claims. And similarly when the legatees testify to that, or two creditors who have a debt against the deceased, or two debtors who owe the deceased, and the two executors testify that he appointed this man along with them. The basis of qiyas: it is testimony by the witness due to benefit returning to him. The basis of istihsan: the judge has the authority to appoint an executor if the person is willing and the death is known, so the judge is spared the burden of identification by this testimony—not that anything is established by it—so it becomes like a lottery. If the two executors admit that there is a third with them, the judge has power to appoint a third with them because they are incapable of acting due to their admission, unlike when the executor denies or death is not known, because he has no authority to appoint an executor, so the testimony itself is the basis. In the case of two debtors who owe the deceased, the testimony is accepted even if death is not known, because they admit against themselves, so death is established in their favor.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the acceptance of testimony about the appointment of an executor (wasi) when the witnesses themselves benefit from the appointment. The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa and his disciples, rules by istihsan (juridical preference) that such testimony is admissible under specific conditions, while the majority of other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) reject it by qiyas (analogy) because the witnesses derive personal benefit. The text presents five scenarios: (1) two sons testify their father appointed an executor, and the executor confirms; (2) the legatees (musa lahu) testify; (3) creditors of the deceased testify; (4) debtors of the deceased testify; (5) two existing executors testify that a third was appointed with them. In all cases, if the executor himself also claims the appointment, the testimony is accepted by istihsan. By qiyas, it would be rejected because the witnesses benefit (e.g., the sons get an executor to manage inheritance, creditors get someone to pay debts, debtors get someone to receive payment, executors get a co-manager). However, istihsan overrides this because the judge has inherent authority to appoint an executor when the death is known (ma'ruf) and a suitable person is willing. The testimony merely helps the judge identify a candidate without needing to search; it does not establish the appointment itself by testimony but rather acts like a lottery (qur'a) to select among candidates. The judge's appointment is independent. If the executor denies, the testimony is rejected because the judge cannot appoint an unwilling person. Similarly, if death is not known, the judge lacks authority, so the testimony would be the sole basis, which is invalid due to self-benefit. An exception is made for debtors: their testimony is accepted even if death is unknown because they are effectively confessing to a debt against themselves, so their admission establishes the death in their own case.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court to establish a fact
وصي (waṣī): Executor appointed by the deceased to manage his estate
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference overriding analogy for a stronger reason
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning from an existing ruling to a new case
قرعة (qur'a): Lottery used to resolve ambiguity, not to establish truth

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the testimony of two sons that their father appointed an executor accepted by istihsan despite the sons benefiting?
A) Because the sons are trustworthy and their benefit is indirect
B) Because the judge has authority to appoint an executor, and the testimony only saves him the effort of identification
C) Because the executor's confirmation makes the testimony admissible
D) Because the death of the father is known by other means

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony that would otherwise be rejected by qiyas, using istihsan, when the judge has independent authority to appoint, making the testimony merely an identification aid.
