نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شہادت دعوی کے موافق نہ ہوگی اور اگر کسی نے دعوی کیا شرقی جانب کی زمین کا اور گواہ نے غربی جانب کی زمین کی گواہی دی تو وضع میں اتحاد نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شہادت دعوئی کے موافق نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر کسی نے دعوی کیا کہ فلاں چیز میری ملک ہے اور گواہ نے گواہی دی کہ اس کے لڑکے کی ملک ہے تو ملک میں اتحاد نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شہادت دعوئی کے موافق نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کسی نے دعویٰ کیا کہ فلاں شخص میرا غلام ہے اس کو میری فلاں باندی نے جنا ہے ۔ گواہ نے گواہی دی کہ اس کے علاوہ دوسری باندی نے جنا ہے تو نسبت میں اتحاد نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شہادت دعوی کے موافق نہ ہوگی۔ بہر حال مذکورہ چیزوں میں اگر اتحاد پایا گیا تو شہادت دعوی کے موافق ہوگی ورنہ مخالف ہوگی۔ اور اس کی وجہ کہ موافقت کی صورت میں شہادت قبول ہوگی۔ اور مخالفت کی صورت میں قبول نہ ہوگی یہ ہے کہ حقوق العباد میں قبولیت شہادت کے لئے دعوئی کا مقدم ہونا شرط ہے اور موافقت کی صورت میں یہ شرط موجود ہے لہذا شہادت قبول ہوگی اور مخالفت کی صورت میں یہ شرط معدوم ہے لہذا شہادت قبول نہ ہو گی۔ رہی یہ بات کہ قبولیت شہادت کے لئے دعوئی کا متقدم ہونا شرط کیوں ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی فصل خصومات کے لئے مقرر ہوتا ہے۔ پس فصل خصومات کے لئے خصومت کا پہلے ہونا ضروری ہے اور خصومت سے دعوی ہی مراد ہے لہذا دعویٰ کا پہلے ہونا ضروری ہوگا۔ اور موافقت کی صورت میں یہ شرط اس لئے موجود ہے کہ شہادت کہتے ہیں دعویٰ کی تصدیق کرنے کو۔ لہذا جب گواہ شہادت دے گا تو گویا وہ دعوی کی تصدیق کرے گا اور تصدیق کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ جس چیز کی تصدیق کی جائے گی وہ پہلے سے موجود ہو۔ پس موافقت کی صورت میں دعوی کا مقدم ہونا پایا گیا اور جب تقدم دعوئی جو قبولیت شہادت کی شرط ہے یا یا گیا تو شہادت بھی قبول ہوگی۔ اور مخالفت کی صورت میں شاہد کا صدق معتبر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مدعی کا ۔ لہذا شاہد جب دعویٰ کی مخالفت کرے گا تو گویا اس نے دعوی کی تکذیب اور تردید کی اور جب دعوی کی تکذیب اور تردید ہوگی تو دعویٰ کا ہونا نہ ہونا برابر ہو گیا۔ اور جب دعویٰ کا ہونا نہ ہو نا برابر ہو گیا تو تقدم دعویٰ جو قبولیت شہادت کی شرط ہے نہیں پایا گیا اور
Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony
The meaning: This chapter is about disagreement in testimony.
Commentary: After discussing the rulings on agreement of witnesses in testimony, the rulings on disagreement in testimony are now being presented. And nature also demands that disagreement in testimony be postponed after agreement in testimony, because agreement is the original and disagreement occurs due to ignorance, falsehood, etc. So since disagreement in testimony is naturally postponed, it has also been postponed in treatment so that correspondence between nature and treatment remains.
Testimony if it agrees with the claim is acceptable, otherwise rejected.
He said: Testimony, if it agrees with the claim, is accepted; and if it contradicts it, it is not accepted, because the precedence of the claim in the rights of human beings is a condition for the acceptance of testimony. And this condition is found in testimony that agrees with the claim and is absent in testimony that contradicts it.
Translation: If testimony agrees with the claim, it will be accepted; if it contradicts the claim, it will not be accepted, because in the rights of people, the precedence of the claim is a condition for the acceptance of testimony. And this condition is found in testimony that agrees with the claim, and is absent in testimony that contradicts it.
Commentary: 'Claim' means demanding one's right in the court of a person who has the authority to relieve [the defendant] after the right is established. Al-Quduri said that testimony, if it agrees with the claim, will be accepted; if it contradicts, it will not be accepted. The meaning of 'agreeing' is that the claim and testimony are unified in terms of type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, reaction, situation, ownership, and relationship. For example, if one person claims ten dinars from another and the witness testifies to ten dirhams, then due to lack of unity in type, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if a person claims ten dirhams from another and the witness testifies to five dirhams, then due to lack of unity in quantity, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if a person claims that another stole a red cloth and the witness testifies to a white cloth, then due to lack of unity in quality, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if someone claims that so-and-so killed my father on the Day of Nahr in Deoband, and the witness testifies that he killed him on the Day of Fitr in Saharanpur, then due to lack of unity in time and place, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if someone claims that so-and-so tore my waterskin and wasted what was inside, and the witness testifies that the waterskin itself tore at the plaintiff's place, then due to lack of unity in action and reaction, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if someone claims land on the eastern side and the witness testifies to land on the western side, then due to lack of unity in situation, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if someone claims that a certain thing is my property and the witness testifies that it is his son's property, then due to lack of unity in ownership, the testimony does not agree with the claim. And if someone claims that so-and-so is my slave born to my such-and-such slave-girl, and the witness testifies that he was born to another slave-girl, then due to lack of unity in relationship, the testimony does not agree with the claim. In any case, if unity is found in the mentioned aspects, the testimony will agree with the claim; otherwise it will contradict. And the reason that in case of agreement the testimony is accepted and in case of contradiction it is not accepted is that in the rights of people, the precedence of the claim is a condition for acceptance of testimony. In case of agreement, this condition exists, therefore the testimony is accepted; in case of contradiction, this condition is absent, therefore the testimony is not accepted. As for why the precedence of the claim is a condition for acceptance of testimony, the reason is that the judge is appointed for deciding disputes. For deciding disputes, the existence of a dispute first is necessary, and by 'dispute' is meant the claim. Therefore, the claim must come first. And in case of agreement, this condition exists because testimony is called confirmation of the claim. So when the witness testifies, he is confirming the claim, and for confirmation it is necessary that the thing being confirmed already exists. So in case of agreement, the precedence of the claim is found, and when the precedence of the claim—which is a condition for acceptance of testimony—is found, the testimony is also accepted. And in case of contradiction, the witness's truthfulness is considered, not the plaintiff's. So when the witness contradicts the claim, he has rejected and denied the claim. And when the claim is rejected and denied, it is as if the claim does not exist. And when the claim's existence becomes null, the precedence of the claim, which is a condition for acceptance of testimony, is not found. And...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on disagreement in testimony (Bab al-Ikhtilaf fi al-Shahada). The commentary first explains the logical order: agreement is the norm, disagreement arises from ignorance or falsehood, so it is treated after agreement. Then the core ruling is stated: testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim (muwafiq al-da'wa); if contradictory, it is rejected. The proof provided is that the precedence of the claim is a condition for acceptance of testimony in cases involving human rights (huquq al-'ibad). The condition is fulfilled when testimony agrees with the claim, but absent when it disagrees. The commentary elaborates on the meaning of 'claim' (da'wa): it is a demand for one's right in the court of a judge who can enforce relief. The passage then enumerates ten aspects in which testimony must match the claim: type (jins), quantity (kamm), quality (kayf), time (zaman), place (makan), action (fi'l), reaction (infi'al), situation (wad'), ownership (milk), and relationship (nisba). Each is illustrated with an example. The underlying rationale is that testimony is a confirmation (tasdiq) of the claim, and confirmation presupposes the pre-existence of what is being confirmed. If the witness contradicts the claim, he effectively denies it, and without a valid claim, the condition of precedence is absent. This passage is a fundamental rule in the law of evidence, ensuring that testimony is relevant and responsive to the claim.

Key Terms
دعوی (da'wa): A claim made by a plaintiff in court demanding a right from the defendant, which, if proven, the judge can enforce.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony given by a witness in court confirming or denying a claim.
موافقت (muwafaqat): Conformity between testimony and claim in type, quantity, quality, time, place, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for testimony to be accepted?
A) The witnesses must be male.
B) The testimony must agree with the claim in ten aspects.
C) The claim must be in writing.
D) The dispute must be over property.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is accepted only if it matches the claim in type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, reaction, situation, ownership, and relationship; otherwise it is rejected.

Agreement of Witnesses: Wording vs. Meaning
Presents the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on witness agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the agreement of witnesses in wording and meaning, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Witnesses must agree on the same fact; but do they need the same words? Abu Hanifa says yes, the Sahibayn say no.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of testimony depends on the agreement of witnesses. But what exactly must they agree on? This lesson presents a classic dispute within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The disagreement centers on whether witnesses must use the same wording (lafz) or merely convey the same meaning (ma'na). Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to assess evidentiary requirements in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa requires for testimony to be accepted. Note his emphasis on both wording and meaning.
This is the stricter view.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the Sahibayn's position: only agreement in meaning is necessary; wording differences do not invalidate the testimony.
They prioritize substance over form.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Sahibayn's analogy to a case where one witness says a thousand and the other says a thousand five hundred. They argue that the common part (a thousand) is established.
They consider the additional part as an isolated increase.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Present Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: different wordings like 'alf' and 'alfayn' are completely different statements, so each witness stands alone. Thus, no single fact has two witnesses.
He emphasizes that meaning is derived from wording.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Show the practical difference: in a claim for two thousand with one witness saying one thousand and the other saying two thousand, Abu Hanifa rejects all, while the Sahibayn accept for one thousand.
This affects whether the plaintiff can establish their claim.

Source Text

گواہوں کا گواہی میں لفظ اور معنا اتفاق معتبر ہے
قال ويعتبر اتفاق الشاهدين فى اللفظ والمعنى عند ابي حنيفة فان شهد احدهما بالف والآخر بالفين لم تقبل الشهادة عنده وعندهما تقبل على الالف اذا كان المدعى يدعى الالفين وعلى هذا المائة والمائتان والطلقة والطلقتان والطلقة والثلث لهما انهما اتفقا على الألف أو الطلقة وتفرد احدهما بالزيادة فيثبت ما اجتمعا لـ عليه دون ما تفرد به احدهما فصار كالالف والالف والخمس مائة ولابى حنيفة انهما اختلفا لفظا وذالك يدل على اختلاف المعنى لانه يستفاد باللفظ وهذا لان الالف لا يعبر به عن الالفين بل هما جملتان متباینتان فحصل على كل واحد منهما شاهد واحد فصار كما اذا اختلف جنس المال
ترجمہ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں گواہوں کا لفظ اور معنی میں متفق ہونا معتبر ہے، پس اگر ان میں سے ایک گواہ نے ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے دو ہزار کی گواہی دی تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ہزار پر گواہی قبول ہو گی بشرطیکہ مدعی دو ہزار کا دعوی کرتا ہو اور اس پر ایک سو، اور دوسو، ایک طلاق اور دو طلاق ، ایک طلاق اور تین طلاق کا اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں گواہوں نے ایک ہزار یا ایک طلاق پر اتفاق کیا اور ایک گواہ زیادتی کے ساتھ متفرد ہے پس جس پر دونوں متفق ہیں وہ ثابت ہو جائیگا اور جن کے ساتھ ان میں سے ایک متفرد ہے وہ ثابت نہ ہوگا پس یہ ایک ہزار اور ڈیڑھ ہزار کے مانند ہو گیا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں گواہوں نے لفظ اختلاف کیا ہے اور یہ معنی کے اختلاف پر دلالت کرتا ہے کیوں کہ معنی لفظ سے مستفاد ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ لفظ الف ( ایک ہزار) سے الفین (دو ہزار) کی تعبیر نہیں ہوتی ہے بلکہ دونوں جملہ جدا جدا ہیں ۔ پس ان میں سے ہر ایک پر ایک گواہ حاصل ہوا لہذا ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جنس مال میں اختلاف کیا ہو۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک گواہوں کا لفظ اور معنی دونوں کے اعتبار سے متفق ہونا ضروری ہے لیکن اگر ترادف کی وجہ سے لفظی اختلاف ہو گیا تو یہ مانع شہادت نہ ہوگا مثلاً ایک گواہ نے میہ کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے عطیہ کی گواہی دی تو یہ گواہی قبول ہوگی اگر چه لفظی اختلاف ہے مگر یہ اختلاف ترادف کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ہبہ اور عطیہ دونوں مترادف ہیں ۔ بہر حال امام صاحب کے نزدیک دونوں گواہوں کا لفظ میں بھی متفق ہونا ضروری ہے اور معنی میں متفق ہونا بھی ضروری ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک صرف معنی میں متفق ہونا ضروری ہے لفظوں میں متفق ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے چنانچہ مدعی نے اگر کسی پر دو ہزار روپیہ کا دعوی کیا اور پھر اس پر مینہ پیش کیا مگر ایک گواہ نے ایک ہزار روپیہ کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے دو ہزار روپیہ کی گواہی دی تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک کمتر پر قبول کرلی جائے گی یہی اختلاف اس وقت ہے جب که مدعی دو سو روپیہ کا دعوی کرے اور اس کا ایک گواہ ایک سو کی گواہی دے اور دوسرا دو سو کی گواہی دے یا بیوی نے دعوی کیا کہ میرے شوہر نے مجھ کو دو طلاقیں دی ہیں مگر گواہوں میں سے ایک نے ایک طلاق کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے دو طلاق کی گواہی دی یا عورت نے تین طلاق کا دعوی کیا مگر ایک گواہ نے ایک طلاق کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے تین طلاقوں کی گواہی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ گواہی باطل ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک کمتر پر قبول کر لی جائینگی۔
Agreement of witnesses in wording and meaning is considered valid. He said: Agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is considered according to Abu Hanifa. If one testifies to a thousand and the other to two thousand, testimony is not accepted according to him. According to them (the Sahibayn), it is accepted for the thousand if the plaintiff claims two thousand. Similarly for one hundred and two hundred, one divorce and two divorces, one divorce and three. For them, they agreed on the thousand or the divorce, and one of them has an increase alone; so what they both agreed upon is established, not what one of them alone added. It becomes like one thousand and one thousand five hundred. And for Abu Hanifa, they differed in wording, and that indicates difference in meaning because meaning is derived from wording. This is because 'alf' (thousand) is not used to express 'alfayn' (two thousand); rather they are two separate sentences. Thus, each has one witness, so it is as if they differed in the type of property. Translation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is considered valid. If one witness testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the testimony is not accepted; according to the Sahibayn, it is accepted for one thousand provided the plaintiff claims two thousand. Similarly, the disagreement applies to one hundred and two hundred, one divorce and two divorces, one divorce and three divorces. The Sahibayn's proof is that the two witnesses agreed on one thousand or one divorce, and one witness is alone with the increase; so what they both agreed upon is established, and what one is alone with is not established. Thus, it becomes like one thousand and one thousand five hundred. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the two witnesses differed in wording, and that indicates difference in meaning because meaning is derived from wording. The word 'alf' (thousand) is not used to express 'alfayn' (two thousand); rather they are two separate sentences. Thus, each has one witness, so it is as if they differed in the type of property. Explanation: Al-Quduri said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is necessary for witnesses to agree in both wording and meaning. But if a wording difference occurs due to synonymy, it does not prevent acceptance. For example, if one witness testifies to 'hiba' (gift) and the other to 'atiya' (gift), the testimony is accepted despite a wording difference because it is due to synonymy; both 'hiba' and 'atiya' are synonymous. In any case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, witnesses must agree in wording and meaning; according to the Sahibayn, they only need to agree in meaning, not wording. Thus, if the plaintiff claims two thousand rupees from someone and brings witnesses, but one testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the testimony is not accepted, while according to the Sahibayn it is accepted for the lesser amount. This same disagreement applies when the plaintiff claims two hundred, and one witness testifies to one hundred and the other to two hundred; or when a wife claims her husband gave her two divorces, but one witness testifies to one divorce and the other to two; or when a woman claims three divorces, and one witness testifies to one divorce and the other to three. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, such testimony is invalid; according to the Sahibayn, it is accepted for the lesser.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the necessary degree of agreement between witnesses. The ruling from al-Quduri states that Abu Hanifa requires witnesses to be unanimous in both the wording (lafz) and the meaning (ma'na) of their testimony. If one witness says 'a thousand' and the other says 'two thousand', Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony entirely, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept it for the lower amount (a thousand) provided the plaintiff claimed the higher amount. The Sahibayn analogize this to a case where one says a thousand and the other says a thousand five hundred—there is common ground on a thousand, so that much is established. Abu Hanifa counters that the words 'a thousand' and 'two thousand' are completely different utterances, so each statement stands alone, resulting in only one witness for each claim—insufficient for proof. The commentary by Al-Quduri adds an important nuance: if the wording difference is due to synonymy, such as 'hiba' and 'atiya' (both mean gift), then Abu Hanifa also accepts the testimony because the meaning is identical even if the words differ. Thus, the core issue is whether wording and meaning are both required, or merely meaning. The practical consequence (thamara) is clear: in cases like claims for money or divorces where witnesses give differing figures, Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony entirely, while the Sahibayn accept it for the lower common figure. This difference affects litigants' ability to prove their claims.

Key Terms
اتفاق (ittifaq): Agreement or unanimity between the two witnesses in their testimony.
لفظ (lafz): The exact wording used by the witness in his testimony.
معنی (ma'na): The intended meaning or subject of the testimony.
ترادف (taraduf): Synonymy; where different words carry the same meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one witness testifies to one divorce and another to two divorces in a case where the wife claims two divorces, what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted for one divorce.
B) The testimony is rejected entirely.
C) The testimony is accepted for two divorces.
D) The testimony is accepted for one and a half divorces.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses must agree on the same fact; the Hanafi school offers two views: Abu Hanifa demands wording and meaning agreement, while the Sahibayn accept meaning agreement alone, with synonymy allowed by all.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Witness Agreement: Wording vs. Meaning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness agreement in wording versus meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding witness agreement in wording and meaning, apply the ruling to scenarios of differing amounts, and identify exceptions like synonymy.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa demands exact wording; the Sahibayn accept meaning alone—the lesser amount stands.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of testimony when two witnesses use different words but refer to the same underlying claim. The source is from Kitab al-Shahada of al-Quduri, with commentary from Ashraf al-Hidaya. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of the Hanafi school's internal methodology and the practical implications for court testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is whether witnesses must agree in both wording (lafẓ) and meaning (maʿnā) or only in meaning. Abu Hanifa requires both, while the Sahibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) require only meaning. In the base case, one witness says 'alf' (1000) and the other says 'alfayn' (2000).
The claimant sued for 2000 in this example.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the witnesses agreed on the lesser amount (1000) in meaning, and the increase is an addition by one witness. They analogize to the case of 1000 and 1500 where the conjunction 'wa' (and) makes it a single expression, so the 1000 is affirmed.
Their dalīl: 'مَا اجْتَمَعَا عَلَيْهِ ثَبَتَ' (what they agreed upon is established).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that different wording indicates different meanings because meaning is derived from wording. 'Alf' and 'alfayn' are separate phrases, so each is supported by only one witness, making the testimony incomplete. This is analogous to a disagreement over the type of property.
His dalīl: 'الاختلاف في اللفظ يدل على اختلاف المعنى' (difference in wording indicates difference in meaning).
4
Apply the dispute to other scenarios
The same principle applies to pairs like 100 and 200, one divorce and two divorces, etc. However, if the verbal difference is due to synonymy (e.g., 'hiba' and 'ʿaṭiyya'), the testimony is accepted because the meaning is identical. Also, when the conjunction 'wa' is used (e.g., 'alf wa khamsa mi'a'), it unifies the expression.
Synonymy and conjunction are exceptions to Abu Hanifa's requirement.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: testimony is accepted for the lesser amount. This is confirmed by the commentary of Ashraf al-Hidaya.
Tarjīḥ authority: The later Hanafi masters preferred the Sahibayn's view for practicality.

رہا یعنی ایک ہزار پر ایک گواہ رہا اور دو ہزار پر ایک گواہ رہا۔ اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ شہادت دو گواہوں کی گواہی کا نام ہے۔ لہذا کسی ایک کے کلام پر بھی شہادت تامہ نہیں پائی گئی ۔ اور جب شہادت قال وان شهد احدهما بالف والآخر بالف وخمس مائة والمدعى يدعى الفا وخمس مائة قبلت الشهادة على الألف لاتفاق الشاهدين عليها لفظا لان الالف والخمس مائة جملتان عطف احداهما على ومعنى الأخرى والعطف يقرر الاول ونظيره الطلقة والطلقة والنصف والمائة والمائة والخمسون بخلاف العشرة والخمسة عشر لانه لي بينهما حرف العطف فهو نظير الالف والالفين
ترجمہ اور اگر دو گواہوں میں سے ایک گواہ نے ایک ہزار کی اور دوسرے گواہ نے ڈیڑھ ہزار کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ڈیڑھ ہزار کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ایک ہزار پر گواہی قبول ہوگی۔ کیونکہ دونوں گواہوں نے ایک ہزار پر لفظ اور معنا اتفاق کر لیا ہے اس لئے کہ ایک ہزار اور
And he (al-Quduri) said: Agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is considered according to Abu Hanifa. So if one of them testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, the testimony is not accepted according to him (Abu Hanifa). But according to them (the two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is accepted for the one thousand if the claimant claims the two thousand. And similarly for one hundred and two hundred, and one divorce and two divorces, and one divorce and three divorces. According to them, they agreed on the one thousand or the one divorce, and one of them is distinguished by the increase, so what they both agreed upon is established, not what one of them distinguished by. So it becomes like one thousand and one thousand five hundred. And according to Abu Hanifa, they differed in wording, and that indicates difference in meaning, because meaning is derived from wording. This is because one thousand is not expressed by two thousand; rather they are two separate phrases. So for each of them, there is one witness, so it becomes as if they differed in the type of property. [The rest is Urdu commentary explaining the dispute and providing examples.]
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Shahada (Book of Testimony) presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the requirement of agreement between witnesses in both wording (lafz) and meaning (ma'na) versus agreement in meaning alone. The author, al-Quduri, states the ruling: Abu Hanifa requires both wording and meaning agreement; the Sahibayn require only meaning agreement. The ruling is illustrated by a case where one witness says 'alf' (1000) and the other says 'alfayn' (2000). Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony entirely because the words differ, implying a difference in what is being testified. The Sahibayn accept it for the lesser amount (1000) because both witnesses agreed on that amount in meaning, and the increase is merely an addition by one witness. The text extends the same principle to other pairs: 100 and 200, one divorce and two divorces, one divorce and three divorces. The Sahibayn provide the example of 1000 and 1500 (alf wa khamsa mi'a), which is accepted by all because the conjunction 'wa' (and) confirms the first number, making the phrase a single expression. Abu Hanifa argues that different words indicate different meanings because meaning is derived from wording; one thousand and two thousand are entirely separate phrases, so each number is attested by only one witness, making the testimony incomplete. The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidaya further explains that a purely verbal difference due to synonymy (e.g., 'hiba' and 'atiyya') does not prevent acceptance because the meaning is the same. The dispute also applies to cases involving different amounts of money or number of divorces, as detailed in the Urdu tashreeh.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony in court by two witnesses to establish a claim.
لفظ (lafz): The actual wording uttered by the witness.
معنى (ma'na): The intended meaning or subject of the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative) position of the Hanafi school, what is the outcome when one witness says '1000' and the other says '2000'?
A) Testimony is rejected entirely.
B) Testimony is accepted for 1000.
C) Testimony is accepted for 2000.
D) The case is dismissed for lack of proper witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, witnesses need only agree on meaning; the lesser amount is accepted, while the increase is ignored.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Dispute on Testimony with Different Amounts: Imam Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony amounts and the role of conjunction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on conflicting testimony amounts, apply the rule of conjunction (atf), and state the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling.

Core Idea
Witnesses must agree in wording and meaning; conjunction 'and' saves the base amount.

In Hanafi jurisprudence, testimony requires two witnesses on the same fact. But what if they testify to different amounts? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-madhhab dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony entirely when the wording differs, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) accept the lesser amount on which both agree. The key turning point is the presence of the conjunction 'and' (waw al-atf), which allows the court to salvage the agreed portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Two witnesses testify to different amounts (e.g., 1000 vs 2000). Does the testimony establish anything, or is it rejected entirely?
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
He rejects the testimony. His dalil: verbal difference (alf vs alfain) implies difference in meaning, and each amount lacks two witnesses. He analogizes to a dispute over the type of property (dirhams vs dinars).
Key principle: 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub' is not used here; it's about wording agreement.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
They accept the lesser amount (1000). Their dalil: both witnesses agree on 1000, so that is established; the extra is supported by only one witness and disregarded. They analogize to the case of 1000 vs 1500 where the lesser is accepted.
4
Analyze the effect of conjunction
When one witness testifies to '1000 and 500' (using waw), the conjunction proves his testimony includes the base 1000, so both witnesses agree on 1000. Without conjunction, the testimony is like '1000 vs 2000' and falls under Abu Hanifa's rejection.
The mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn when conjunction is present.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If 1000 vs 2000 without conjunction: Abu Hanifa rejects entirely; Sahibayn accept 1000. If 1000 vs 1000 and 500 with conjunction: the ruling is accept 1000 by agreement.
The judge must check the exact wording of the testimony.

گواہی بالا تفاق قبول کر لی جاتی ہے لہذا اسی طرح مذکورہ مسئلہ میں بھی کم تر مقدار پر گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب ایک گواہ نے ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے دو ہزار کی گواہی دی تو دونوں نے لفظا اختلاف کیا ہے۔ اور اختلاف لفظ دلالت کرتا ہے اختلاف معنی پر کیوں کہ معنی لفظ ہی سے مستفاد ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب لفظوں میں اختلاف ہو گیا تو معنی میں بھی اختلاف ہوگا اور اختلاف لفظ اختلاف معنی پر اس وجہ سے بھی دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مثلاً لفظ الف ( ایک ہزار ) سے دو ہزار کی مقدار کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا ہے اور لفظ الفین (دو ہزار سے ایک ہزار کی مقدار کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔ پس دونوں گواہوں میں سے ہر ایک کا کلام دوسرے کے کلام کے مغائر ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے کلام کا مدلول دوسرے کے کلام کے مدلول کا مغائر اور مبائن ہے۔ اور جب یہ بات ہے تو ہر کلام پر ایک گواہ رہا یعنی ایک ہزار پر ایک گواہ رہا اور دو ہزار پر ایک گواہ رہا۔ اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ شہادت دو گواہوں کی گواہی کا نام ہے۔ لہذا کسی ایک کے کلام پر بھی شہادت تامہ نہیں پائی گئی ۔ اور جب شہادت تامہ نہیں پائی گئی تو اس کو قبول بھی نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے گواہوں نے جنس مال میں اختلاف کیا ہو۔ مثلاً ایک گواہ نے ہزار درہم کی اور دوسرے نے ایک سود بینار کی گواہی دی ہو تو یہ گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی۔ پس اسی طرح ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار کے اختلاف کی صورت میں بھی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
قال وان شهد احدهما بالف والآخر بالف وخمس مائة والمدعى يدعى الفا وخمس مائة قبلت الشهادة على الألف لاتفاق الشاهدين عليها لفظا لان الالف والخمس مائة جملتان عطف احداهما على ومعنى الأخرى والعطف يقرر الاول ونظيره الطلقة والطلقة والنصف والمائة والمائة والخمسون بخلاف العشرة والخمسة عشر لانه لي بينهما حرف العطف فهو نظير الالف والالفين
ترجمہ اور اگر دو گواہوں میں سے ایک گواہ نے ایک ہزار کی اور دوسرے گواہ نے ڈیڑھ ہزار کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ڈیڑھ ہزار کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ایک ہزار پر گواہی قبول ہوگی۔ کیونکہ دونوں گواہوں نے ایک ہزار پر لفظ اور معنا اتفاق کر لیا ہے اس لئے کہ ایک ہزار اور

اشرف الہدایہ جلد- و ہم وة
كتاب الشهادة
پانچ سو د و جملہ ہیں ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا دوسرے پر عطف کیا گیا ہے اور عطف اول کو ثابت کرتا ہے۔ اور اس کی نظیر ایک طلاق اور ڈیرہ طلاق ہے اور ایک سو اور ڈیڑھ سو ہے۔ برخلاف دس اور پندرہ کے اس لئے کہ ان کے درمیان حرف عطف نہیں ہے۔ پس یہ ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار کی نظیر ہے۔
تشریح گزشتہ مسئلہ میں گزر چکا ہے کہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک شاہدین کا لفظ اور معنی میں متفق ہونا قبولیت شہادت کی شرط ہے۔ اس پر متفرع کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر دونوں گواہوں میں سے ایک نے ایک ہزار درہم کی گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے ایک ہزار پانچ سو درہم کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ڈیڑھ ہزار کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے تو ایک ہزار درہم پر گواہی قبول ہو جائیگی ۔ اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار پر لفظا بھی متفق ہیں اور معنی بھی متفق ہیں۔ معنی متفق ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ پڑھ ہزار کے ضمن میں ایک ہزار بھی موجود ہے۔ اور لفظ انفاق اس لئے ہے کہ الالف والخمس مائة( ایک ہزار اور پانچ سو ) دو جملہ ہیں۔ دوسرے جملہ کا پہلے جملہ پر عطف کیا گیا ہے یعنی خمس مائة کا الف پر عطف گیا ہے۔ اور عطف اول یعنی معطوف علیہ کو ثابت کرتا ہے۔ لہذا جس گواہ نے ایک ہزار اور پانچ سو کی گواہی دی اس نے بھی اولا ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی ہے۔ پس ایک ہزار پر دونوں گواہوں کا اتفاق پایا گیا۔ اور جب ایک ہزار پر دونوں گواہ لفظ اور معنا دونوں طرح متفق ہو گئے تو قبولیت شہادت کی شرط پائی جانے کی وجہ سے ایک ہزار پر گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک گواہ نے کسی کی طرف سے ایک طلاق کی گواہی دی اور ایک نے ایک طلاق اور نصف طلاق کی گواہی دی اور مدعی ایک اور نصف طلاق کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ایک طلاق ثابت نہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر ایک گواہ نے ایک سو درہم کی گواہی دی اور ایک نے ایک سو پچاس درہم کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ایک سو پچاس کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ایک سو درہم کی گواہی ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔لیکن اگر ایک گواہ نے دس درہم کی گواہی دی اور ایک نے پندرہ درہم کی گواہی دی تو چونکہ خمسة عشر میں خمسة اور عشر کے درمیان حرف عطف نہیں ہے اس لئے خمسة عشر ایک حکم ہوگا اور خمسة عشر ، اور صرف عشر کے درمیان تبائین ہوگا پس گویا ایک گواہ نے جس پر گواہی دی ہے دوسرے نے اس کے خلاف پر گواہی دی ہے۔ اور جب ایسا ہے دونوں گواہوں کا متفق ہونا نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور جب گواہوں کا اتفاق نہ ہوسکا تو گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ پس یہ ایک ہزار دو ہزار کی نظیر ہے۔ فوائد... ایک ہزار اور ایک ہزار پانچ سو کی صورت میں ایک ہزار پر اور ایک سو اور ایک سو پچاس کی صورت میں ایک سو پر گواہی اس وقت قبول ہوگی جبکہ یہ عبارت عربی میں ہو یا اردو میں حرف واڈ درمیان میں لائے ۔ مثلاً یوں کہے ایک ہزار اور پانچھو ، ایک سو اور پچاس۔ اور اگر اردو کے محاورہ کے مطابق گواہ ایک ہزار پانچ سو یا پندرہ سو کہے یا ڈیڑھ ہزار کہے تو گواہی قبول نہ ہونی چاہئے جیسے ایک سو پچاس یا ڈیڑھ سو کہنے میں یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ قبولیت شہادت کا مدار حرف عطف پر تھا اور وہ اس صورت میں پایا نہیں گیا۔ جمیل

وان قال المدعى لم يكن لى عليه الا الالف فشهادة الذي شهد بالالف والخمس مائة باطلة لانه كذبه المدعى فى المشهود به وكذا اذا سكت الا عن دعوى الالف لان التكذيب ظاهر فلابد من التوفيق ولو قال كان اصل حقى الفا وخمس مائة ولكني استوفيت خمس مائة او ابراته عنها قبلت لتوفيقه
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Bidayah vol. 10. The Sahibayn's argument is that both witnesses have agreed on the lesser amount: in the text's case, on one thousand; in the commentary's case, on one hundred; and on one divorce. Both witnesses are agreed. However, one witness added an extra: in the text's case, an extra thousand; in the commentary's case, an extra hundred; and an extra one or two divorces. So when the witnesses agree on the amount – that is, one thousand, or one hundred, or one divorce – that amount is established. And the amount to which only one witness testified – i.e., the extra thousand, extra hundred, or extra one or two divorces – that amount is not established because the witness remains alone (for that part). An example of this is: if one person claims one thousand five hundred rupees from another, but one witness testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand five hundred, then because the witnesses have agreed on one thousand in wording and meaning, the testimony on one thousand is accepted by agreement. Similarly, in the mentioned case, the testimony on the lesser amount will be accepted. Imam Abu Hanifa's argument is that when one witness testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, they have verbally differed. And verbal difference indicates difference in meaning, because meaning is derived from words. So when the words differed, meaning also differs. Verbal difference indicates difference in meaning also because, for example, the word 'alf' (one thousand) does not express the amount of two thousand, and the word 'alfain' (two thousand) does not express the amount of one thousand. So the speech of each witness contradicts the speech of the other, because the import of each speech is contradictory and opposite to the import of the other. When this is the case, each statement has only one witness: for one thousand, one witness; for two thousand, one witness. And it has already passed that testimony is (requires) the testimony of two witnesses. Therefore, complete testimony is not achieved for any single statement. And when complete testimony is not achieved, it will not be accepted. This is like the witnesses differing in the type of property: e.g., one witness testifies to one thousand dirhams and the other to one dinar. Such testimony is not accepted. Similarly, in the case of disagreement between one thousand and two thousand, testimony will not be accepted. He said: If one of them testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand five hundred, and the plaintiff claims one thousand five hundred, the testimony is accepted for the one thousand because the witnesses agree on it verbally. Because 'one thousand and five hundred' are two sentences; one is conjoined to the other, and the conjunction confirms the first. Its analogy is one divorce and one and a half divorces, and one hundred and one hundred fifty. Unlike ten and fifteen, because there is no conjunction between them. So this is analogous to one thousand and two thousand. Translation: And if from two witnesses, one testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand five hundred, and the plaintiff also claims one thousand five hundred, the testimony is accepted for the one thousand. Because both witnesses have agreed on one thousand in wording and meaning. Because one thousand and five hundred are two sentences; one is conjoined to the other, and the conjunction affirms the first. Its analogy is one divorce and one and a half divorces, and one hundred and one hundred fifty. Unlike ten and fifteen, because there is no conjunction between them. So this is analogous to one thousand and two thousand. Explanation: It has passed in the previous issue that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, agreement of witnesses in wording and meaning is a condition for acceptance of testimony. Based on this, he said: If from two witnesses, one testifies to one thousand dirhams and the other to one thousand five hundred dirhams, and the plaintiff claims one thousand five hundred, then the testimony on one thousand dirhams is accepted. The reason is that both witnesses agree on one thousand both verbally and in meaning. Agreement in meaning is obvious because the one thousand is included within the one thousand five hundred. And verbal agreement is because 'alif wa khoomsi mi'a' (one thousand and five hundred) are two sentences; the second is conjoined to the first, i.e., 'khoomsi mi'a' is conjoined to 'alif'. And the conjunction confirms the first, i.e., the conjoined-to. Therefore, the witness who testified to one thousand and five hundred has also firstly testified to one thousand. So there is agreement of both witnesses on one thousand. And when they agreed on one thousand both verbally and in meaning, the condition for acceptance of testimony is met, so testimony on one thousand is accepted. Its analogy is: if one witness testifies to one divorce from someone, and the other testifies to one and a half divorces, and the plaintiff claims one and a half divorces, then one divorce is established. Similarly, if one witness testifies to one hundred dirhams and the other to one hundred fifty dirhams, and the plaintiff also claims one hundred fifty, then testimony on one hundred dirhams is established. But if one witness testifies to ten dirhams and the other to fifteen dirhams, then because 'fifteen' has no conjunction between 'five' and 'ten', 'fifteen' is one unit and there is contradiction between 'fifteen' and just 'ten'. So it is as if one witness testified to something and the other testified to its opposite. When this is the case, the witnesses' agreement is not found. And when their agreement is not found, testimony is not accepted. This is analogous to one thousand and two thousand. Benefits: In the case of one thousand and one thousand five hundred, testimony on one thousand is accepted, and in the case of one hundred and one hundred fifty, testimony on one hundred is accepted, provided that the wording is in Arabic or in Urdu with the conjunction 'and'. For example, say 'one thousand and five hundred', 'one hundred and fifty'. But if according to Urdu idiom the witness says 'one thousand five hundred' or 'fifteen hundred' or 'one and a half thousand', then testimony should not be accepted, just as in saying 'one hundred fifty' or 'one and a half hundred', the same ruling applies, because the acceptance of testimony depends on the conjunction, and it is not found in that case. And if the plaintiff says: 'I only had one thousand owed to me by him', then the testimony of the one who testified to one thousand and five hundred is void, because the plaintiff has accused him of lying in what was testified. Similarly, if he is silent about the claim of one thousand, because the accusation of lying is apparent. So reconciliation (between the witnesses) must be achieved. And if he says: 'My original right was one thousand five hundred, but I have received five hundred or I have remitted it to him', then the testimony is accepted because he has reconciled.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key dispute in the Hanafi school regarding testimonies when witnesses differ on the amount. The lesson type is an inter-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The central issue: if one witness testifies to 1000 and another to 2000, what is the ruling? The Sahibayn argue that since both agree on the lesser amount (1000), that amount is established, and the extra is disregarded because only one witness supports it. They draw an analogy to a case where one witness says 1000 and the other says 1500; they agree on 1000. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees: the testimony is rejected entirely because the witnesses have verbally differed (alf vs. alfain). For him, verbal difference indicates a difference in meaning, and since testimony requires two witnesses on the same fact, complete testimony is not achieved. He compares this to differing in the type of property (dirhams vs. dinars). The passage then examines a specific scenario: one witness says 1000, the other says '1000 and 500' (using the conjunction 'and'). Here, the ruling is to accept the testimony on 1000 because the conjunction shows that the witness also testified to 1000 (the first part). This is distinguished from the case of '10 and 15' where there is no conjunction, so it is like the '1000 vs 2000' case. The commentary emphasizes that the acceptance depends on the presence of the conjunction 'and' (waw). If the witness says 'one thousand five hundred' as a single phrase without 'and', it is like the rejected case. Finally, if the plaintiff denies the extra amount, the testimony of the witness who claimed the extra is void, unless the plaintiff reconciles by stating that he had the extra but later forgave or received it. The mufta bihi position is the Sahibayn's view in cases with conjunction, as the text adopts that ruling.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court, requiring two witnesses on the same fact.
عطف (atf): Grammatical conjunction (waw) that joins two phrases, indicating that both parts are testified by the same witness.
اختلاف لفظ (ikhtilaf lafz): Difference in wording between witnesses, which according to Imam Abu Hanifa indicates difference in meaning and invalidates testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if one witness testifies to 1000 dirhams and the other to 2000 dirhams (without conjunction), what is established?
A) 2000 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) Nothing; the testimony is rejected
D) Both amounts are established

Key Takeaway
When witnesses differ on the amount, the lesser amount is established (Sahibayn's view, mufta bihi) provided there is agreement in wording, which is confirmed by the presence of a conjunction.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony with Discrepancy in Amount: Conjuncted Excess
Ruling on accepting testimony when witnesses differ by a conjuncted excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on testimony when witnesses differ in amount to determine the common amount established, and distinguish between cases with and without a conjunctive phrase.

Core Idea
When witnesses' statements differ by a conjuncted excess, the common base amount is established in testimony.

In Hanafi testimony law, acceptance of testimony requires witnesses to agree in both wording and meaning. But what happens when one witness states a base amount and the other adds an excess with a conjunction? This lesson unpacks a ruling from al-Hidayah that shows how the conjunction allows separation, affirming the base amount as a shared element. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly applying the conditions of testimony in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two testimonies
Note each witness's exact wording. Look for a conjunction ('and') that connects an additional amount to a base amount.
Example: 'one thousand' vs. 'one thousand and five hundred'.
2
Determine if the excess is conjuncted
Check if the excess is introduced by a conjunction (atf) that separates it from the base. If so, the statement is two separate clauses.
In Arabic/Urdu, the conjunction 'و' (and) or Urdu 'اور' indicates separation.
3
Separate the base from the excess
The conjuncion affirms the first part (the base). Thus the witness who stated the combined amount also testified to the base amount.
The excess is not part of the agreed testimony; only the base is common.
4
Check agreement on the base
Both witnesses must agree on the base amount in wording and meaning. Here, they do: the first states one thousand, the second also states one thousand (as the first part of his compound statement).
Agreement in meaning is also satisfied because the base is included in the larger amount.
5
State the ruling
Testimony is accepted for the common base amount. The excess is not established by the testimony and must be proven separately if claimed.
This ruling also applies to other analogous cases, e.g., divorce or other amounts.

Source Text

گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے ایک ہزار پانچ سو درہم کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ڈیڑھ ہزار کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے تو ایک ہزار درہم پر گواہی قبول ہو جائیگی ۔ اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار پر لفظا بھی متفق ہیں اور معنی بھی متفق ہیں۔ معنی متفق ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ [پڑھ] ہزار کے ضمن میں ایک ہزار بھی موجود ہے۔ اور لفظ انفاق اس لئے ہے کہ الالف والخمس مائة( ایک ہزار اور پانچ سو ) دو جملہ ہیں۔ دوسرے جملہ کا پہلے جملہ پر عطف کیا گیا ہے یعنی خمس مائة کا الف پر عطف گیا ہے۔ اور عطف اول یعنی معطوف علیہ کو ثابت کرتا ہے۔ لہذا جس گواہ نے ایک ہزار اور پانچ سو کی گواہی دی اس نے بھی اولا ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی ہے۔ پس ایک ہزار پر دونوں گواہوں کا اتفاق پایا گیا۔ اور جب ایک ہزار پر دونوں گواہ لفظ اور معنا دونوں طرح متفق ہو گئے تو قبولیت شہادت کی شرط پائی جانے کی وجہ سے ایک ہزار پر گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک گواہ نے کسی کی طرف سے ایک طلاق کی گواہی دی اور ایک نے ایک طلاق اور نصف طلاق کی گواہی دی اور مدعی ایک اور نصف طلاق کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ایک طلاق ثابت نہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر ایک گواہ نے ایک سو درہم کی گواہی دی اور ایک نے ایک سو پچاس درہم کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ایک سو پچاس کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ایک سو درہم کی گواہی ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔لیکن اگر ایک گواہ نے دس درہم کی گواہی دی اور ایک نے پندرہ درہم کی گواہی دی تو چونکہ خمسة عشر میں خمسة اور عشر کے درمیان حرف عطف نہیں ہے اس لئے خمسة عشر ایک حکم ہوگا اور خمسة عشر ، اور صرف عشر کے درمیان تبائین ہوگا پس گویا ایک گواہ نے جس پر گواہی دی ہے دوسرے نے اس کے خلاف پر گواہی دی ہے۔ اور جب ایسا ہے دونوں گواہوں کا متفق ہونا نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور جب گواہوں کا اتفاق نہ ہوسکا تو گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ پس یہ ایک ہزار دو ہزار کی نظیر ہے۔ فوائد... ایک ہزار اور ایک ہزار پانچ سو کی صورت میں ایک ہزار پر اور ایک سو اور ایک سو پچاس کی صورت میں ایک سو پر گواہی اس وقت قبول ہوگی جبکہ یہ عبارت عربی میں ہو یا اردو میں حرف واڈ درمیان میں لائے ۔ مثلاً یوں کہے ایک ہزار اور پانچھو ، ایک سو اور پچاس۔ اور اگر اردو کے محاورہ کے مطابق گواہ ایک ہزار پانچ سو یا پندرہ سو کہے یا ڈیڑھ ہزار کہے تو گواہی قبول نہ ہونی چاہئے جیسے ایک سو پچاس یا ڈیڑھ سو کہنے میں یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ قبولیت شہادت کا مدار حرف عطف پر تھا اور وہ اس صورت میں پایا نہیں گیا۔ جمیل
Chapter of Testimony. Five hundred and one thousand are two sentences. One is attached to the other with a conjunction, and the conjunction affirms the first. Its analogy is one divorce and one and a half divorces, and one hundred and one hundred and fifty. Unlike ten and fifteen, because there is no conjunction between them. So this is analogous to one thousand and two thousand. Commentary: In the previous issue it was mentioned that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the requirement for acceptance of testimony is that the witnesses agree in wording and meaning. Building on that, he said: If one of the two witnesses testifies to one thousand dirhams and the other testifies to one thousand five hundred dirhams, and the claimant also claims one thousand five hundred, then the testimony is accepted for one thousand dirhams. The reason is that both witnesses agree on one thousand both in wording and meaning. Agreement in meaning is obvious because one thousand is included in one thousand five hundred. As for wording, because 'one thousand and five hundred' are two sentences, with 'five hundred' attached to 'one thousand' by conjunction. And the conjunction affirms the first (the conjoined item). Therefore, the witness who testified to one thousand and five hundred also testified first to one thousand. Thus both witnesses agree on one thousand. When both witnesses agree on one thousand in wording and meaning, the condition for acceptance is met, so testimony is accepted for one thousand. Its analogy is: if one witness testifies to one divorce and another to one and a half divorces, and the claimant claims one and a half divorces, then one divorce is established. Similarly, if one witness testifies to one hundred dirhams and another to one hundred fifty, and the claimant claims one hundred fifty, then one hundred dirhams is established. But if one witness testifies to ten dirhams and another to fifteen, then because in 'fifteen' there is no conjunction between 'five' and 'ten', 'fifteen' is a single term, and there is contradiction between fifteen and ten alone. So it is as if one witness testified to something and the other to the opposite. Hence, there is no agreement, and testimony is not accepted. This is analogous to one thousand and two thousand. Benefits: In the case of one thousand and one thousand five hundred, acceptance on one thousand, and in the case of one hundred and one hundred fifty, acceptance on one hundred, occurs only when the expression is in Arabic or in Urdu with the conjunction 'and'. For example, say 'one thousand and five' or 'one hundred and fifty'. If according to Urdu idiom the witness says 'one thousand five hundred' or 'fifteen hundred' or 'one thousand and a half', then testimony should not be accepted, just as in saying 'one hundred fifty' or 'one hundred and a half', the same ruling applies, because acceptance of testimony depends on the conjunction, and it is not found in these expressions. Jameel.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a commentary on a ruling from al-Hidaya regarding a discrepancy in the amount testified by two witnesses. The author expands on the principle that for testimony to be accepted, the witnesses must agree in both wording (lafzan) and meaning (ma'nan). The specific case: one witness says 'one thousand dirhams', the other says 'one thousand and five hundred dirhams', and the claimant claims one thousand five hundred. The ruling: testimony is accepted for one thousand dirhams. The reasoning shows that the first witness's statement is one thousand; the second witness's statement 'one thousand and five hundred' is two separate sentences joined by a conjunction. The conjunction affirms the first part (one thousand). Therefore, both witnesses agree on one thousand in wording and meaning. The excess (five hundred) is not part of the agreed testimony. The author provides analogies with divorce (one divorce vs. one and a half divorces) and money (one hundred vs. one hundred fifty) to illustrate the point. He contrasts this with the case of ten and fifteen, where 'fifteen' is a single compound word without a conjunction, so there is no agreement on ten. The passage also includes a beneficial note (fa'idah): the conjunction condition applies only when the amount is expressed with a conjunction (e.g., 'one thousand and five hundred'). If the witness says 'one thousand five hundred' or 'fifteen hundred' without a conjunction, testimony is not accepted because there is no separation of the amounts. This highlights the importance of wording in testimony acceptance.

Key Terms
عطف (atf): Grammatical conjunction (e.g., 'and') that connects two phrases, affirming the first.
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given by witnesses in court.
توافق (tawāfuq): Agreement between witnesses in the subject of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses in a debt case: one says 'I testify that he owes 1000 dirhams', the other says 'I testify that he owes 1000 and 500 dirhams'. The claimant claims 1500 dirhams. What amount is established by their testimony?
A) Nothing, because they disagree on the total.
B) 500 dirhams.
C) 1000 dirhams.
D) 1500 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses differ by a conjuncted excess, the common base amount - agreed in both phrasing and meaning - is established in testimony; the excess requires separate proof.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Claimant's Denial on Discrepant Testimony
Ruling when claimant denies or is silent about the extra amount in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a claimant's denial (takdhib) of a part of a witness's testimony invalidates that witness's entire testimony, and distinguish it from the rule of iqrar (confession) where 'adalah is not required.

Core Idea
Claimant's denial of a witness's extra amount makes the witness a fasiq, invalidating all his testimony—unlike confession.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key issue in testimony law: what happens when a claimant directly or implicitly denies part of a witness's testimony? The ruling hinges on the concept of takdhib, which impugns the witness's 'adalah (uprightness). In contrast, in cases of confession (iqrar), such denial does not affect the confessor's statement. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the qiyas to iqrar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the matn carefully: claimant denies the extra amount, claimant is silent about the extra amount, and claimant provides a reconciliation (tawfiq). Note the ruling for each.
The matn uses specific phrasing: 'wa in qala', 'idha sakat', 'law qala'.
2
Understand the hukm and its reason
For the first two scenarios, the witness who testified to the larger amount is rejected. The reason is takdhib: the claimant's denial effectively accuses the witness of lying, rendering him fasiq. A fasiq's testimony is inadmissible.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that 'adalah is a condition for testimony.
3
Analyze the qiyas objection and response
The text presents an objection: why not accept the witness's testimony on the common amount, as in iqrar? The Hanafi response distinguishes: in testimony, the witness must be 'adl; in iqrar, the confessor's 'adalah is not required, so denial does not invalidate.
This highlights a key difference between shahada and iqrar in Hanafi law.
4
Apply the rule to silence
When the claimant is silent about the extra amount (only claims the lesser amount), it constitutes implicit denial. The same ruling applies: the witness's testimony is invalid because takdhib is apparent.
Silence here is not neutral; it is treated as denial because the claim is inconsistent with the testimony.
5
Recognize the effect of tawfiq
If the claimant provides a plausible explanation (e.g., he had a larger original claim but collected part), the testimony is accepted. This is because the discrepancy is resolved—the witness spoke truthfully about the original, and the claimant explained the reduction.
Tawfiq restores the witness's credibility; the judge rules based on the claimant's actual claim, not the full testimony.

بھی قبول کر لی جائیگی اور قاضی ایک ہزار پر اپنا فیصلہ دید یگا۔
besturdubooks.wordpress.com
And if the claimant said: 'I had nothing against him except one thousand', then the testimony of the one who testified to one thousand and five hundred is invalid, because the claimant himself denied him in the testified matter. Similarly, if he remained silent except about the claim of one thousand, because the denial is apparent, so reconciliation is necessary. But if he said: 'My original right was one thousand and five hundred, but I recovered five hundred or I absolved him from it', then it is accepted due to reconciliation. Translation: And if the claimant said: 'I had nothing against the defendant except one thousand', then the testimony of the person who testified to one thousand and five hundred is invalid, because the claimant himself has denied him in the testified amount. Similarly, if he remained silent except about the claim of one thousand, because denial is apparent, so reconciliation is necessary. And if the claimant said: 'My original right was one thousand and five hundred, but I recovered five hundred or I absolved the defendant from it', then due to this reconciliation, the testimony is accepted. Commentary: The scenario is: if one of the two witnesses testifies to one thousand and another to one thousand five hundred, and the claimant claims that he had nothing against the defendant except one thousand, then the testimony of the one who testified to one thousand five hundred becomes invalid. After it becomes invalid, only one witness remains on the claim, and the testimony of one witness proves nothing, so even the one thousand is not established through only one person's testimony. The testimony of the one who testified to the excess is invalid because the claimant himself denied the amount he testified to. So after the claimant's denial, what question arises of accepting his testimony? But there is an objection: the claimant only denied the five hundred, not the one thousand. Therefore, his testimony on one thousand should be considered, and the judge should decide one thousand, just as if someone confessed to one thousand five hundred rupees for another, but the confestee denied the five hundred and affirmed the one thousand, then the judge decides one thousand rupees. The answer to this is that the claimant denied the witness, so he effectively declared him a transgressor (fasiq), and the testimony of a fasiq is not admissible. Therefore, the testimony of this witness is not admissible. As for the other witness, he is alone, so no decision is made on his testimony. As for the confession, the confessor does not need to be 'adl, so even if the confestee declares him fasiq, his confession is valid and the judge decides accordingly. Similarly, if the claimant claimed one thousand and remained silent about the rest, neither affirming nor denying, then also the judge will not decide one thousand for the claimant, because when the claimant claimed one thousand, he effectively denied the five hundred of the witness who testified to one thousand five hundred. The point is that in this case too, denial from the claimant is apparently established. When denial from the claimant is established, without reconciliation between the claimant's claim and the witness's testimony, the testimony will not be accepted. And when one witness's testimony is not accepted, the other witness being alone, no decision is made on his testimony. Yes, if the claimant said: 'My original right was one thousand five hundred, but I have recovered five hundred rupees or I have absolved the defendant from five hundred rupees', then due to reconciliation between the claimant's own claim and the witness's testimony, the testimony is accepted. That is, there is harmony: the witness testified to the original matter (one thousand five hundred), and the claimant stated an intervening event (he received or forgave five hundred). The witness was not aware of this, so the claimant claimed one thousand. Thus, due to harmony, the testimony given for one thousand five hundred is also accepted, and the judge will give a decision for one thousand.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the effect of the claimant's own statement on discrepant testimony. The Arabic matn presents three scenarios: (1) The claimant says he was owed only one thousand (denying the extra amount). Then the testimony of the witness who said one thousand five hundred is invalid. (2) The claimant remains silent about the extra amount, only claiming one thousand — same ruling because silence implies denial. (3) The claimant explains the discrepancy by saying his original right was one thousand five hundred but he either recovered or forgave five hundred. Then the testimony is accepted because the claimant reconciles his claim with the witness's testimony. The Urdu commentary elaborates: When the claimant denies the extra amount, he effectively accuses the witness of lying, which renders the witness a fasiq (sinner) in the eyes of the court. A fasiq's testimony is not accepted at all. Therefore, that witness's testimony is entirely rejected. The other witness is alone, and one witness's testimony is insufficient to prove anything. The commentary addresses an objection: why not accept the second witness's testimony on the one thousand, similar to the case of iqrar (confession)? The distinction is that in testimony, the witness must be 'adl (upright). When the claimant denies the extra amount, he impugns the witness's character, making him fasiq. In iqrar, the confessor does not need to be 'adl; so even if the confestee calls him a liar, his confession is still effective. The commentary also clarifies that if the claimant is silent about the extra amount, it is treated as implicit denial, so the same ruling applies. Finally, if the claimant provides a plausible reconciliation (that he had a larger original claim but collected part of it), then the witness's testimony is accepted for the larger amount, but the judge only rules based on what the claimant claims (one thousand).

Key Terms
تکذیب (takdhīb): Denial or accusation of lying by the claimant against a witness.
توفیق (tawfīq): Reconciliation between the claimant's claim and the witness's testimony by providing a plausible explanation.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession or admission of a right against oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses: one testifies to one thousand dirhams, another to one thousand five hundred dirhams. The claimant says: 'I only had one thousand dirhams against the defendant.' What is the ruling?
A) Testimony is accepted for one thousand dirhams from both witnesses
B) The second witness's testimony is invalid, and only one witness remains, so nothing is proven
C) Both testimonies are accepted for one thousand five hundred dirhams
D) The second witness's testimony is accepted for one thousand dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a claimant denies any part of a witness's testimony, the witness becomes fasiq and his entire testimony is rejected; reconciliation can only save it if the claimant provides a plausible explanation.

Effect of Plaintiff's Contradiction on Witness Testimony: The 1000/1500 Case
Ruling with proof and objection-response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a plaintiff's contradiction (takdhib) of a witness renders the witness fasiq and invalidates his entire testimony, and distinguish this from the case of confession (iqrar).

Core Idea
Plaintiff's contradiction makes the witness fasiq, so his whole testimony is rejected.

This passage examines a common testimony scenario: the plaintiff claims 1000, one witness confirms 1000, and another claims 1500. The plaintiff's explicit or implicit denial of the extra 500 has a drastic effect. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi condition that witnesses must be 'adil and how the plaintiff's takdhib destroys that condition. The passage also contrasts testimony with confession, where 'adalah is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the facts and plaintiff's claim
Start with the scenario: plaintiff claims 1000, witness A says 1000, witness B says 1500. Note that the plaintiff's claim is an implicit contradiction of the 500 excess if he remains silent, or explicit if he says 'only 1000 was owed'.
2
Apply the takdhib rule to witness B
The plaintiff's contradiction of the 500 renders witness B fasiq (unreliable). Hanafi law: a fasiq's testimony is invalid. Therefore witness B's entire testimony (including the 1000 part) is rejected.
3
Consider the objection and the counter-argument
A student might object: why not accept the uncontradicted 1000 part? The passage answers by distinguishing testimony from confession. In testimony, the witness's 'adalah is a condition; in confession, the confessor's 'adalah is not required. Hence partial contradiction invalidates a witness but not a confessor.
4
Evaluate the exception: tawfiq
If the plaintiff explains that the original debt was indeed 1500 but he received 500 or forgave it, there is no contradiction. The witness testified to the original debt, and the plaintiff explains a subsequent event. This reconciliation (tawfiq) restores the witness's testimony because the witness is not contradicted.
5
Derive the final ruling
Without tawfiq, only one valid witness remains (witness A). One witness is insufficient to prove the claim, so no judgment is given. With tawfiq, witness B is accepted, and the judge may rule for 1000 based on both witnesses.

بھی قبول کر لی جائیگی اور قاضی ایک ہزار پر اپنا فیصلہ دید یگا۔
Testimony chapter. Translation: If plaintiff says that the defendant owed him nothing more than 1000, then the testimony of the person who testified to 1000 and 500 is invalid because the plaintiff himself contradicted (takhdhib) him regarding the extra 500. Similarly, if he remained silent about the extra 500, the takdhib is apparent. So reconciliation (tawfiq) is necessary. But if plaintiff says his original right was 1500 but he received 500 or forgave the defendant 500, then due to tawfiq the testimony is accepted. Explanation: The case is that one witness testified 1000 and another 1500, and plaintiff claimed only 1000. The 1500 witness's testimony is invalid because plaintiff contradicted him. Only one witness remains, so 1000 is not proven either. Objection: Plaintiff contradicted only the 500 excess, not the 1000, so the 1000 part should be accepted, similar to a case where someone confesses to 1500 but the confesse contradicts 500 and confirms 1000. Answer: By contradicting, plaintiff declared the witness fasiq, and fasiq's testimony is not accepted, unlike confession where 'adalah is not required. If plaintiff claims 1000 and stays silent, the same applies. However, if plaintiff says his original right was 1500 but he received 500 or forgave it, then there is no contradiction because the witness testified about the original debt and plaintiff about a subsequent event, so the testimony is accepted for 1000.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a witness testifies to an amount greater than what the plaintiff claims. The passage is a commentary expanding on a ruling from the matn. The key point: if the plaintiff explicitly contradicts the witness regarding the extra amount, the witness's entire testimony becomes invalid because the plaintiff's contradiction effectively declares the witness unreliable (fasiq). The objection that the contradiction only applies to the extra amount is answered by distinguishing between testimony and confession: in testimony, the witness must be 'adil, and calling him fasiq invalidates his entire testimony; in confession, the confessor's 'adalah is not required, so partial contradiction does not invalidate the uncontradicted part. If the plaintiff reconciles by explaining that the original debt was indeed the larger amount but he received part, then the testimony becomes acceptable because there is no contradiction regarding the original debt.

Key Terms
تکذیب (takdhib): Contradiction or denial by the plaintiff of the witness's testimony regarding the amount.
توفیق (tawfiq): Reconciliation between plaintiff's claim and witness's testimony by explaining a subsequent event (e.g., payment or forgiveness).
فاسق (fasiq): A person who is legally unreliable, whose testimony is rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a plaintiff claims 1000, witness A testifies to 1000, and witness B testifies to 1500, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) Witness B's testimony is accepted for 1000 but not for the extra 500.
B) Witness B's testimony is completely invalid, so only one witness remains, and no judgment is given.
C) The judge decides that 1500 is owed because two witnesses agree on 1500?
D) The plaintiff must pay witness B's expenses for bringing false testimony.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi testimony law, a plaintiff's contradiction (takdhib) of a witness on any part renders the witness fasiq and invalidates his entire testimony, unless the plaintiff provides reconciliation (tawfiq).

One Witness Adds Payment: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Ruling on testimony where one witness adds a payment claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the authoritative Hanafi position when one witness adds a payment claim, distinguish it from Abu Yusuf's view, and apply the distinction between initial agreement and subsequent unsupported claims.

Core Idea
A single witness cannot prove payment if both witnesses agree on the principal debt.

This lesson examines a subtle dispute within the Hanafi school. When two witnesses both confirm a debt of 1000, but one of them later states that 500 has already been paid, does the judge accept the full 1000 or only 500? The answer hinges on the difference between contradicting the original testimony and adding an unsupported separate fact. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying testimony rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the facts
Two witnesses agree on a debt of 1000. One witness adds that 500 was paid. Note that the principal amount is undisputed between the witnesses; the extra claim is about a separate event.
2
State the matn's ruling
The base text says the testimony for 1000 is accepted, and the statement of payment is not heard because it is a single witness's claim. So judge rules for 1000.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that the witness claiming payment effectively testifies that only 500 is owed, creating a disagreement (1000 vs 500). By qiyas with the case where one says 1000 and another says 2000, the judge should rule for the lower amount (500).
4
Follow Imam Muhammad's rebuttal
Imam Muhammad responds that in the 1000 vs 2000 case, one witness initially testifies to the lower amount. Here, both initially testify to 1000, so there is no disagreement on the principal. The payment claim is an additional fact that does not contradict the original testimony; it is merely unsupported.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
Al-Hidayah sides with Imam Muhammad, making the relied-upon position: rule for 1000. The payment claim is ignored unless corroborated by another witness or evidence.

كتاب الشهادة
گواہوں نے مدعی کے حق میں ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی ایک گواہ نے کہا مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ پانچ سوادا کر دیئے ہیں تو دونوں کی گواہی ہزار میں قابل قبول ہے پانچ سو کی گواہی مردود ہوگی
قال واذا شهدا بالف وقال احدهما قضاه خمسمائة قبلت شهادتهما بالالف لاتفاقهما عليه ولم يسمع قوله انه قضاه خمس مائة لانه شهادة فرد الا ان يشهد معه آخر وعن أبي يوسف انه يقضى بخمسمائة لان شاهد مون شهادته ان لا دين الا. مس مائة وجوا
الق
قلنا
ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں گواہوں نے ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی اور اُن میں سے ایک نے کہا کہ مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کو پانچ سوادا کر دیتے ہیں تو ہزار پر دونوں کی گواہی قبول ہوگی کیونکہ اس مقدار پر دونوں گواہ متفق ہیں اور گواہ کا قول کہ مدعی عالیہ نے مدعی کو پانچ سوادا کر دئیے ہیں مسموع نہ ہوگا۔ کیوں کہ یہ ایک شخص کی گواہی ہے مگر یہ کہ دوسرا شخص اسکے ساتھ ہو اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ پانچ سوکا حکم کیا جائے گا کیونکہ پانچ سو درہم ادا کرنے کی گواہی دینے والے گواہ کی شہادت کا مضمون یہ ہے کے قرضہ صرف پانچ سو درہم ہے اور اس کا جواب وہی
سے جو ہم نے کہا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کسی دوسرے شخص پر ایک ہزار روپیہ کا دعوی کیا اور دو گواہوں نے مدعی کے حق میں ایک ہزار روپیہ کی گواہی دیدی مگر ایک گواہ نے کہا کہ مدعی علیہ ان میں سے پانچ سورو پیادا کر چکاتے تو ایک ہزار پر دونوں کی گواہی قبول ہو جائے گی اور ایک گواہ کا یہ کہنا کہ مدعی علیہ نے پانچ سورو پیادا کردیے ہیں مسموع اور قابل قبول نہ ہوگا۔ ایک ہزار پر دونوں کی گواہی تو اس لئے مقبول ہوگی کہ دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار روپیہ پر متفق ہیں اور پانچ سورو پیادا کرنے کا قول اس لئے قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا کہ یہ فقط ایک شخص کی گواہی ہے حالانکہ ایک شخص کی گواہی سے کوئی حق ثابت نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے لیکن اگر دوسرا شخص بھی اس کے ساتھ ہو اور پانچ سو روپیہ ادا کرنے کی گواہی دے تو گواہی قبول ہو جائے گی ۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ قاضی صرف پانچ سوروپیہ کا حکم دیگا یعنی اس شہادت کے نتیجہ میں مدعی علیہ پر صرف پانچ سورو پیادا کرنا واجب ہو گا۔
اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس گواہ نے پانچ سورو پید ادا کرنے کی گواہی موی ہے اس کی گواہی کا مضمون یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کے ذمہ فقط پانچ سو روپیہ کا قرضہ ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا ایک گواہ نے ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی ہے اور دوسرے نے پانچ سو رو پید کی گواہی دی ہے سورہ اور ایسی صورت میں قاضی مقدار اقل پر فیصلہ دینے کا مجاز ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ اگر گواہوں نے ایک ہزار دو ہزار میں اختلاف کیا ہو تو صاحبین کے نزدیک اقل یعنی ایک ہزار پر فیصلہ دے دیا جائے گا پس اسی طرح یہاں بھی مقدار اقل یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ کا فیصلہ دے دیا جائیگا لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں امام محمد امام یوسف کے خلاف ہیں اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ شاہدین کے مقدار اقل اور مقدار اکثر میں اختلاف کرنے سے مقدار اقل کا حکم اس وقت دیا جاتا ہے جبکہ ایک گواہ نے ابتداء مقدار اقل پر شہادت دی ہو جیسا کہ الف اور الفین کے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں یہ بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس مسئلہ میں یہ ہے کہ ابتدا ، دونوں گواہوں نے ایک ہزار پر گواہی دی مگر بعد میں جب پانچ سورو پیادا کرنے کی گواہی دے دی تو گویا اس نے یہ کہا کہ مدعی کے مدعی عالیہ پر صرف پانچ سوروپیہ واجب الادا ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب وہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں یعینی
Ashraf al-Hidayah volume 10, page 103, book of testimony. Two witnesses testified for 1000; one said defendant had paid 500. So both testimonies are acceptable for 1000 because they agree on that; the statement that 500 was paid is not heard because it is testimony of a single person, unless another joins him. From Abu Yusuf: judgment is given for 500 because the witness who testifies to payment effectively denies any debt beyond 500. Our answer is what we said. Translation: If both witnesses testify to 1000 and one says defendant paid 500, then both testimonies for 1000 are accepted because they agree; the witness's statement of payment is not heard because it is a single testimony unless another joins. From Abu Yusuf: judgment is given for 500 because the witness's testimony implies the debt is only 500. The answer is the same as we said. Explanation: A person claimed 1000, two witnesses testified for 1000, but one said defendant paid 500. Testimony for 1000 is accepted; the statement of payment is not accepted because it is only one witness. If another joins, it would be accepted. Abu Yusuf says judge rules for 500 because the witness's testimony implies only 500 is owed. His proof: it is as if one witness testified to 1000 and another to 500, and the judge may rule for the lower amount, as in the case of 1000 vs 2000. However, Imam Muhammad disagrees, saying that rule applies only when one witness initially testifies to the lower amount; here both initially testified to 1000, so the extra statement of payment does not reduce the principal. The author of Hidayah says the answer to Abu Yusuf's argument is what we have already stated.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the effect of one witness's additional statement that part of the debt was paid. The authoritative matn states that if two witnesses both testify to 1000, and one adds that 500 was paid, the testimony for 1000 is accepted because both agree on that amount. The statement of payment is not accepted because it is a solitary testimony. However, Abu Yusuf argues that the witness who claims payment is effectively testifying that only 500 is owed, thus there is disagreement between the witnesses (1000 vs 500), and the judge should rule for the lower amount (500), analogous to the case where witnesses disagree on 1000 vs 2000. Imam Muhammad rebuts this: in the 1000 vs 2000 case, one witness initially testified to 1000; here both initially testified to 1000, and the statement of payment is an additional claim that does not contradict the original testimony—it is simply an unsupported claim of payment. The author of Hidayah sides with Imam Muhammad, as indicated by 'our answer is what we said.'

Key Terms
شهادة فرد (shahadat fard): Testimony of a single witness, which is insufficient to prove a right in most cases.
اقل (aqall): The lower amount when witnesses disagree; the judge may rule for the lower amount as a compromise.
قضاء (qada'): Judgment or fulfillment of a debt (in this context, payment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where two witnesses testify to a debt of 1000 and one adds that 500 was paid, what is the ruling according to the authoritative Hanafi position?
A) The testimony for 1000 is invalid because of the disagreement.
B) The judge rules for 500, following Abu Yusuf's opinion.
C) The testimony for 1000 is accepted and the statement of payment is ignored.
D) The judge requires a third witness to decide.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi testimony law, the claim of payment by a single witness does not override the agreed principal debt; it requires independent proof.
